The factory's ONLY legitimate definition of 'improved' is: it can now one-shot, or build faster/cheaper, a basket of past intents it previously fumbled — proven by re-running them headless against current code/skills/prompts. A self-change that makes replays worse is rolled back; self-improvement PRs that don't beat the vault don't exist. **Why better:** The current 'improve when friction repeats 5x' has no ground truth — it chases whatever hurt most recently and can 'improve' the factory into being worse on jobs it used to nail. A held-out replay suite gives improvement an objective, regression-proof, rollback-able target.
- **Andon cord + poka-yoke: any worker can halt the line and the stoppage becomes a permanent mistake-proofing jig** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Steal Toyota: give every headless worker an andon cord — when it hits a problem it judges systemic (not just its own leaf), it halts the swarm, and the orchestrator must either auto-generate a poka-yoke (a lint rule, contract assertion, test scaffold, template guard) that makes that defect structurally impossible, or escalate. The poka-yoke is committed back into the golden templates. **Why better:** The current loop tolerates the SAME failure 5 times before acting, wasting 4 runs of spend. Andon + poka-yoke stops the bleeding on the first systemic defect AND engineers it out at the template/contract level so it literally cannot recur — defect-prevention, not defect-counting.
- **Champion/challenger shadow factory: every self-change must beat the incumbent on real runs to ship** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Steal ML A/B + canary/blue-green: run two versions of the factory's own config (prompts, router policy, templates) at once. The champion handles real runs; each self-evolution proposal becomes a challenger that shadow-builds the same leaves in a parallel worktree. Promote the challenger ONLY when it beats the champion on cost+speed+green-rate over N real runs; otherwise auto-discard. **Why better:** The current loop drafts a refactor with no proof it's better and leaves a human to judge on faith — so improvements rot un-merged or get merged blind. Champion/challenger makes self-improvement EARN promotion against the incumbent on real workloads — a rigorous, automatic, regression-safe path to actually evolve.
- **Blameless postmortems auto-mined into a queryable Runbook the graph serves, governed by an error budget** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Steal Google SRE: after every run (success OR failure) an agent writes a structured blameless postmortem — what the plan got wrong, which contract was underspecified, which model lost the bet — into graphify, so the FIRST thing every future worker queries before grepping is 'has the factory been burned doing exactly this before?'. Pair it with an error budget: if recent runs burn too much, the factory auto-throttles the altitude dial (biases SMALLER, more gates) until reliability recovers. **Why better:** The friction ledger stores only opaque failure CODES with counts — it can't tell a future worker WHY or HOW to avoid it. Postmortems-in-the-graph give workers natural-language institutional memory they can reason over, and the error budget gives the 'bias BIGGER' dial a self-correcting governor.
- **Remote build cache for whole leaves — learn from every SUCCESS, instantly, with zero LLM judgment** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Steal Bazel/Nx/Turborepo: hash every leaf's CONTRACT (typed signature + schema + failing tests + golden template + model version) and store the green built artifact in a content-addressed remote cache keyed by that hash. The next run of ANY factory — any user, any project — that produces a leaf with an identical contract hash gets an instant cache HIT and skips the model spend; only true misses dispatch a worker. **Why better:** The current loop only learns from FAILURES (repeated 5x). A build cache learns from every success immediately with no LLM judgment, and makes 'factory builds factories' literal: a new run inherits the whole org's prior green work for free instead of re-deriving it.
- **A co-evolving Red Factory — an adversary that hunts the build-factory's failures before any user does** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Stand up a second Codex-driven 'factory' whose sole job is to author intents and contracts the build-factory currently FAILS to satisfy (subtle schema traps, race conditions, contradictory contracts, ambiguous scopes, specs designed to slip past tests). Any case where tests go green but the artifact is actually wrong becomes a new mandatory invariant / contract rule / gate. The build-factory improves by closing each gap; the red factory improves by finding new ones — self-improvement as a two-factory arms race instead of a friction timer. **Why better:** Single-model self-judgment is circular — the same priors that built the work grade it, and friction only reports failures users already hit. A separately-evolving adversary manufactures failure proactively and cheaply in a sandbox, so the factory's defenses are shaped by the worst case, not by whatever broke this week.
- **The Factory forks itself and runs an evolutionary tournament against itself** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — On every idle cycle the factory clones its own source into N worktrees, mutates a different subsystem in each (router heuristics, contract-freezing rules, leaf-classification, stitch order), then sends a fixed battery of real build requests — or the regression vault — through all variants in parallel. The variant that ships more green artifacts per token wins, its mutation merges back to trunk, and losers are culled and archived as ablations (a map of what NOT to try again). The factory is literally subject to natural selection against itself. The conservative pole of this is the same machinery with frozen, hand-versioned variants and an A/B ship-gate pick instead of in-place mutation — giving clean rollback and an honest counterfactual. **Why better:** A single self-evolution branch is a guess with no control group — you can't prove it helped and there's no clean rollback. Tournament forks make improvement empirical and parallel (more processes = more power, the factory's own thesis), discover wins that were never bottlenecks, and prove them on real workloads instead of one Codex's guess.
- **Twin factories that diverge, specialize, and trade genes** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Run two long-lived factory lineages on different objective weightings — one biased toward speed/cost, one toward correctness/polish — and let them evolve independently for weeks. Periodically they swap their best-performing subsystems (horizontal gene transfer) and a meta-judge keeps whichever hybrid dominates on a shared benchmark. Speciation as an explicit strategy for not getting stuck in one local optimum. **Why better:** A single self-improving factory hill-climbs toward one local maximum and can't tell it's stuck. Divergent lineages explore different regions of the design space and recombine, escaping plateaus a single-thread reactive loop would never leave.
- **The Factory publishes its own changelog and defends each self-edit to a cross-model jury** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Every self-edit must ship with a factory-written rationale, a before/after benchmark on real builds, and a cross-model defense where Claude proposes and Codex prosecutes (or vice versa). Only edits that survive the adversarial jury AND beat their own benchmark get merged; the full argument is kept as a queryable audit trail of why the factory is the way it is. **Why better:** Today's flow drafts a branch and stops — a human still has to figure out if it's good, with no record of reasoning. A self-justifying, jury-gated changelog makes autonomous self-merge trustworthy and gives the owner a readable history of the factory's evolution.
- **INVERT: delete self-improvement — ship a frozen factory with hand-versioned releases** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Kill the 'factory improves itself over time' assumption entirely. The factory is a normal product: it ships at v1.0, improvements come from YOU reading run logs and editing skills/templates by hand, released as v1.1, v1.2. No live self-modification loop at all — just a changelog, and a version a user can pin. **Why better:** A self-improving factory stacks two hard problems (build artifacts AND build the builder), and the second has no error signal you trust. A frozen hand-versioned factory is debuggable, reproducible, and pinnable. ArtLab already refuses to auto-merge its self-evolution drafts — that instinct taken to its conclusion says the loop shouldn't exist, only the human-reviewed release.
- **INVERT: outsource self-improvement to the two models — the factory stays dumb** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Build zero self-improvement machinery. Claude and Codex get better between releases for free. The factory pins to whatever the frontier models can do this quarter and contributes no learning of its own — its 'improvement' is entirely a function of the model upgrade you didn't build and don't maintain. **Why better:** The biggest capability jumps come from the model vendors, not an in-house learned-heuristic store that depreciates the moment the next model ships. Building self-improvement machinery competes with — and is obsoleted by — the model roadmap. Bet on the exponential you don't own over a linear one you hand-roll.
- **INVERT: the factory builds ONE thing well and refuses to generalize itself** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — The opposite of 'factory builds factories' is 'factory refuses to be a meta-tool.' Hard-code it to The Tower's stack and domain only. It never abstracts its own contracts/templates into a reusable engine; every improvement is a Tower-specific patch, not a generalization. **Why better:** Premature generalization is the classic meta-system failure — you pay the abstraction tax before you have three real users of the abstraction. A parochial factory gets the golden templates exactly right for one stack instead of mediocre for all. 'Universal' is the seductive trap; specific-and-excellent beats general-and-fuzzy until proven otherwise.
- **INVERT: the factory should DEGRADE by default — append-only with forced pruning** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Assume the opposite of 'gets better': left alone, accumulated skills, templates, and learned heuristics rot and conflict. Build the inverse mechanism — mandatory decay. Every learned rule has a TTL and must re-earn its place against fresh runs or it's auto-deleted. The system's default trajectory is shrinking, not growing. **Why better:** Self-improving systems usually self-degrade in practice (cruft, contradictory learned rules, prompt bloat) — 'improvement' is the marketing word for accumulation. Designing for forced entropy keeps the factory lean and confronts the real failure mode head-on, instead of assuming a magic upward ratchet that doesn't exist.
- **INVERT: collapse 'self-improvement' into graphify — it's not a separate aspect** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — There is no 'self-improvement' aspect; there is only the graph getting more accurate. Every 'the factory learned something' event is really 'graphify recorded an as-built fact or a failure pattern.' Delete self-improvement as a standalone concept, cockpit panel, and roadmap line — it's just graph enrichment. **Why better:** Naming it 'self-improvement' invites scope creep, anthropomorphism, and a roadmap item impossible to scope or finish. Reframing as 'the graph is more correct than yesterday' is concrete, measurable (drift between contract graph and reality shrinks), and already owned by an aspect you're building anyway. One fewer system to maintain.
- **INVERT: point the recursion at a KILL SWITCH, not at more capability** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — The one self-referential thing the factory should build for itself is containment, not capability: self-generated guardrails, scope fences, and abort conditions. The only sanctioned meta-loop is the factory making itself easier to STOP, not easier to expand. **Why better:** An autonomous orchestrator spawning headless workers with zero human interaction is exactly where a runaway-cost or runaway-scope incident lives. Pointing the recursive instinct at safety turns the most dangerous property (self-modification) into the most reassuring one — the only meta-feature whose failure mode is 'too safe' rather than 'unbounded spend.'
- **INVERT: self-improvement is a vanity metric — measure the factory only by shipped artifacts** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Forbid the factory from optimizing itself; let it optimize OUTPUT only. No internal 'how good is the factory' score, no learned-skill leaderboard, no meta-dashboard. The single number is: did the artifact pass tower-ship-gate, first try, this run? Improvement, if it happens, is an emergent side effect nobody is allowed to target directly. **Why better:** Optimizing the meta-layer (Goodhart on 'factory quality') diverts effort from the only thing the user pays for: finished artifacts. Tying every change to a first-pass ship-gate rate keeps the loop honest and starves the tempting-but-unfalsifiable 'the system is learning' narrative of oxygen.

### Shared-resource contention & write serialization

_Current assumption: The seed treats parallel workers as embarrassingly independent ('more processes = more power'), assuming git worktrees give clean isolation. Unstated: many leaves are NOT independent — they touch the SAME shared singletons (the Drizzle schema file, the DB migration sequence, the Tailwind config, package.json, the route manifest, an enum, a barrel export). The factory has no concept of a per-resource WRITE LEASE or serialization point. ArtLab already learned this the hard way (slot-leases, engine-level lock, no-duplicate-spend) but the factory hypothesis silently assumes worktree isolation makes contention disappear. It doesn't: two leaves both adding a column to the same migration, or both editing the schema barrel, collide at stitch time. Who owns the lock on shared mutable surfaces?_

**Boldest reframe:** The schema/migrations/manifest/configs/barrels DO NOT EXIST as writable files during the build — they are DERIVED at stitch time by projecting each leaf's local, self-contained declaration into the global file. You cannot have a write-contention problem on a file nobody is allowed to write. This is the boldest because it doesn't answer 'who holds the lock' — it deletes the locked object. Every other strong idea (CRDTs, stewards, append-only logs, single-writer reducers, codegen'd singletons) is a specific implementation of this one reframe; this is the reframe itself, stated at its most absolute: workers emit only intents, the factory generates every shared surface, and humans/leaves never edit them. Contention becomes structurally unrepresentable rather than scheduled, leased, or merged away.

- **Declare the shared-singleton set explicitly in the manifest** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Maintain a small named registry of the ~7 real shared mutable surfaces — src/db/schema.ts, the migration sequence + meta/_journal.json, tailwind.config.ts, package.json, the route/app tree, each pgEnum, each barrel export — as first-class manifest entities. Every leaf's contract must DECLARE which of these it will touch (its write-set) before the swarm starts, the same way it declares typed signatures. **Why better:** The hypothesis treats every file as independent and discovers collisions only at stitch time. Naming the handful of real singletons (confirmed: schema.ts is one 1086-line file imported by 17 files; migrations share one _journal.json) turns invisible contention into a declared, inspectable property of each leaf — the conflict graph becomes visible before a single token is spent.
- **Stitch-time conflict pre-flight: graph-color the write-sets at plan-freeze** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Before dispatching workers, run a static contention-coloring pass over the frozen contracts. Each leaf declares its read-set and write-set of surfaces; leaves sharing a write-surface get the same 'color' and are forced sequential, disjoint colors run in parallel — exactly like register allocation / Nx affected-graph. The scope-preview gate renders the coloring as RED nodes: 'these 4 leaves all serialize on schema.ts — split or sequence.' **Why better:** The current model conflates 'in separate worktrees' (filesystem isolation) with 'touches disjoint surfaces' (semantic isolation) and only checks the first. Coloring moves contention discovery from the most expensive moment (after the parallel spend, when the green wave hits an unmergeable conflict) to the cheapest (the existing free scope gate). graphify already wants the contract graph; this just adds write-edges and reads them as a scheduler input.
- **Per-resource write lease — lift ArtLab's setIfAbsent lease store to code surfaces** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Promote ArtLab's proven slot-lease primitive (confirmed in repo: InMemory/FileCreativeSlotLeaseStore with compare-and-swap setIfAbsent, heartbeatAtMs/timeoutMs, and stale-lease reconciliation) into a CodeSurfaceLeaseStore. A worker must acquire a write-lease on a fine-grained key like 'db/schema.ts:enum:application_status' or 'tailwind.config:theme.colors' before it may emit a write to that surface; one lease per surface; no lease, no write; stale leases auto-reclaimed on crash. The stitcher REFUSES any patch whose author didn't hold a valid unexpired lease for every resource it touched. **Why better:** The hypothesis says ArtLab 'learned this the hard way' then re-imports the bug it already fixed. This is the literal lesson, already coded, tested, and crash-hardened in this repo. Serializing only the few hot surfaces keeps 'more processes = more power' true for the 95% that touch nothing shared, and a stitcher that verifies lease tokens converts 'hope the merge is clean' into an enforced invariant.
- **Append-only everything: forbid in-place mutation of shared singletons; fold fragments deterministically** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Workers may only APPEND, never edit. Each leaf drops a uniquely-named fragment — 0042_leaf-warroom_add_priority_col.sql, schema/tables/applications.partial.ts, a one-line enum-value file, a single route-entry file. The 'real' schema, migration sequence, barrel, route manifest, and configs are a deterministic FOLD over the fragments, ordered by a topological dependency stamp rather than edit time. Two differently-named appends never touch the same bytes. **Why better:** The migration directory already proves this: 41 migrations, zero locks, because nobody rewrites 0041. Append-only is collision-free by construction. The entire class of 'both edited the same migration / same barrel line / same enum' evaporates; the only residue is a pure deterministic sort, not a human-mediated merge.
- **Shard the monolith: one-table-per-file schema so most leaves never share a surface** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — The factory's FIRST act on any DB-touching campaign is to explode src/db/schema.ts into src/db/tables/<table>.ts (plus schema/enums.ts) re-exported by a GENERATED barrel. 'Add column to orders' and 'add table interviews' become edits to DIFFERENT files — genuinely independent worktree writes. Each leaf is assigned its own file. Contention collapses to only the tiny generated barrel and the migration sequence. **Why better:** Confirmed: 32 tables/enums live in one 1086-line file purely by Drizzle convention, not requirement (Drizzle composes a schema from many files). The contention here is FALSE sharing manufactured by layout. Partitioning by domain restores the seed's 'embarrassingly parallel' assumption for the 90% case cheaply, instead of building heavyweight arbitration for a problem the file structure created.
- **Pre-mint the contested namespace: allocate migration ordinals, enum values, route slugs, and IDs at contract-freeze** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Contract-freezing pre-allocates every contested identifier and hands each leaf a reservation: 'your migration is ordinal 0042, your enum value is order_status.refunded, your route is /refunds, your barrel slot is N' BEFORE it runs. Leaves build against reservations like a build system handing out monotonic job IDs, rather than each independently inventing names/positions at build time. **Why better:** Prevents the specific SILENT corruptions a generic file-merge produces happily: duplicate enum value, two leaves both minting 0042 against a stale _journal.json, two routes claiming the same path. Trades a cheap allocation pass for eliminating an undebuggable class of stitch-time conflicts — and a stale _journal.json is exactly why two drizzle-kit generate runs can't be git-merged.
- **Lease-aware altitude classifier: fold co-contending leaves UP into one worker** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — When the altitude dial detects that several sibling leaves all declare the same singleton surface, automatically MERGE them into one larger parent leaf owned by a single worker, rather than splitting them. The dial already biases bigger — make shared-surface contention an explicit reason to bias bigger. **Why better:** Splitting one schema change across three workers who all need schema.ts creates three-way contention for negative benefit. The cheapest serialization is the one you design out by never splitting in the first place: folding co-contending leaves into one node eliminates the lock entirely for that surface.
- **The DB already owns serialization — emit migration INTENTS, let Postgres+drizzle-kit collapse them** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Don't build a factory-level write-lease for the migration sequence. The thing that actually applies migrations (Postgres advisory locks + drizzle-kit's migrations table) is already a crash-safe transactional serialization point. Leaves emit migration INTENTS ('add column status to applications'); a single apply step at the boundary collapses them into ordered, numbered SQL. The orchestrator holds zero opinions about migration locking. **Why better:** A worktree-level JSON lease with a 10-minute staleness window is a leaky imitation of a guarantee Postgres already gives for free, transactionally, and crash-survivably. Reusing the DB's existing serialization is strictly more correct than re-inventing a lease that can go stale mid-write.
- **Mutex zones in the dispatcher: serialize the contended ~10%, parallelize the disjoint ~90%** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Group leaves by the resource fingerprint they touch into 'mutex zones': all leaves writing the schema barrel share a zone and run sequentially within it; leaves in disjoint zones stay maximally parallel. The orchestrator's dispatcher reads these zones off the manifest, exactly like Nx/Turborepo compute the affected sub-graph and parallelize only what's provably independent. **Why better:** Today the dispatcher fans out blindly on the 'embarrassingly parallel' assumption and pays at stitch. Mutex zones keep ~90% of the parallelism (most leaves ARE disjoint) while serializing only the genuinely-shared 10% — the Turborepo win, applied to the build swarm.
- **Type-aware union-merge for additive surfaces (enums, barrels, route arrays)** `small/rash` _(curated)_ — For the small class of ADDITIVE shared surfaces — a pgEnum's value list, a barrel's export list, a route-manifest array, a feature-flag map — provide a structured 3-way union-merger so two leaves each adding one entry both win, instead of one clobbering the other or producing a textual conflict. **Why better:** Plain git merge treats two appends to the same enum or export list as a conflict even though they're semantically commutative. A type-aware union-merge lets these additive cases stay fully parallel and auto-stitch cleanly, capturing the easy 80% of 'collisions' that aren't real conflicts at all.
- **Optimistic concurrency with version stamps + automatic rebase-and-retry of the loser** `small/rash` _(curated)_ — Drop all upfront locks. Every shared resource carries a version stamp (an ETag / a row's xmin). A worker reads the stamp at start; at stitch the engine compares. If the surface advanced underneath it, the LOSER leaf is automatically re-run by a fresh headless process against the NEW base — its contract and failing tests are unchanged, only the base moved. Winners commit immediately. Serialize only on actual collision, exactly like a DB MVCC engine instead of a global table lock. **Why better:** Pessimistic locking serializes every leaf that MIGHT touch schema.ts even when they touch disjoint tables — throughput death; and a pessimistic lease can stall the swarm when contention is rare. OCC keeps the embarrassingly-parallel speed and pays the cost only on the rare true collision. And because each leaf is one-shot-regenerable to a frozen contract, 'rebase the loser' is cheap here in a way it never is for human PRs — it matches the factory's own bet that leaves are cheap to re-spawn.
- **Let it collide, then let the green wave arbitrate the merge mechanically** `small/rash` _(curated)_ — Drop all leases. Workers freely write whatever they want to their own worktree copy of schema.ts. At stitch, collisions surface as merge conflicts and the climbing green-wave verification RESOLVES them mechanically: re-derive the barrel from declarations, renumber migrations 0042/0043 in commit order, union the enums. Contention is handled optimistically at the JOIN, not pessimistically at the FORK. **Why better:** Locks pay a coordination cost on EVERY shared-surface write even though most runs have few real conflicts. Optimistic resolution pays only when a conflict actually happens, and the stitch phase is the natural, already-existing place to renumber migrations and regenerate barrels deterministically.
- **Shard the namespace per-leaf so no surface is ever singular** `small/rash` _(curated)_ — Invert 'shared mutable surface' into 'no surface is shared': give every leaf a private namespace — prefixed enum values, per-feature route subtrees, per-leaf migration files numbered by leaf-ID-hash not a global counter, scoped Tailwind layers. The collision disappears not because access is coordinated but because the surface was never singular. **Why better:** A lease serializes access to ONE name; sharding gives everyone a DIFFERENT name so serialization is unnecessary. It trades a hard, stateful, race-prone runtime coordination problem for a static naming convention that's checkable at plan time and free at runtime.
- **Migration-sequence broker: one node owns the number line** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Treat the numbered migration sequence (0000…0041 plus meta/_journal.json) as a single-writer append-only log owned by a dedicated 'migration broker' / 'migration-sequencer' node, stealing the Kafka/Temporal single-writer-per-partition pattern. Leaves never run drizzle-kit generate in their own worktree — they submit a desired schema delta, and the broker serially assigns the next number, appends the journal entry, and folds all deltas into one ordered migration. **Why better:** Worktree isolation is exactly what BREAKS here, confirmed by structure: two leaves each run drizzle-kit generate, both produce 0042_*.sql against a stale _journal.json, and the result is git-unmergeable because the sequence is inherently serial. A single broker makes the one genuinely non-parallel resource explicit and conflict-free by construction — the move manufacturing made when it stopped letting every station stamp its own part number.
- **Single-writer steward actors: one privileged agent per shared surface, everyone else sends typed requests** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Capability becomes asymmetric. Spin up one long-lived single-threaded owner-actor per shared mutable surface — a Schema Steward, Migration Steward, Manifest/Route Steward, package.json Steward, Theme Steward (the actor model / VFX 'one lighting lead owns the master rig'). Build leaves can READ any surface but may only file typed REQUESTS into a steward's mailbox ('I need column x:int on table y', 'I claim route /floor/8'). The steward serializes, dedupes, emits ONE coherent change in dependency order, and returns a stable typed handle (the new enum value, the new export name) the leaf codes against. **Why better:** Turns an N-way race into a 1-writer-per-resource actor model — the classic, boring, correct serialization point the seed says is missing. A surface with exactly one writer can never have a write-write race. Replaces 'acquire the right lock and hope everyone cooperates' (which fails the moment one worker forgets — locks are advisory and bypassable) with 'only one process CAN write, so corruption is unrepresentable.' Ownership is explicit, singular, and auditable: 'who holds the lock' becomes 'who do you ask.'
- **Resources are first-class plan-tree nodes with owners, assigned at plan time (Bazel/Nx targets)** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — During top-down contract-freezing, every shared mutable surface (schema file, migration sequence, tailwind.config, package.json, each barrel export, each enum) is promoted into an explicit RESOURCE NODE in the graphify graph with an owner field. A leaf doesn't 'edit the schema' — it declares a typed edge 'needs-write: schema/applications'. Bazel/Nx do exactly this: every file an action touches is a declared input/output, and the scheduler refuses to run two actions that declare a write to the same output. Two leaves wanting the same surface is a PLANNING conflict the architect resolves before any process spawns. **Why better:** ArtLab's lease lives at runtime because contention was discovered DURING execution — because the plan modeled WORK (leaves) but never the SURFACES work mutates. Promoting surfaces to owned nodes turns an undetectable runtime race into a statically-visible graph edge the orchestrator can serialize, lease, or reject BEFORE spending a token. Makes 'who owns the lock' a designed answer in the manifest instead of an emergent race.
- **Contention is a planning bug: pre-partition every singleton into disjoint ownership so collisions are structurally impossible** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — There is NO write-lease, no serialization point, no runtime lock — because if two leaves ever touch the same migration sequence or schema barrel at the same time, the PLAN-TREE was malformed. Contract-freezing pre-partitions every shared singleton into disjoint ownership BEFORE the swarm starts, so at build time no two workers CAN collide because no two were ever handed the same surface. **Why better:** A lock makes contention a thing you survive at runtime (queue, retry, stitch-time merge). Moving it to plan time makes contention structurally impossible — the orchestrator can PROVE zero collisions before spending a single token, instead of discovering them after the parallel spend is gone.
- **Absorb contention into the contract-freeze: the contract IS the pre-resolved patch to every singleton** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — There is no standalone 'write serialization' subsystem at all. Frozen contracts ALREADY enumerate every typed signature, every DB column, every enum value top-down — so the set of shared-surface writes is fully known at freeze time. Fold contention entirely into the contract: the contract literally is the pre-resolved, conflict-free patch to every singleton (the schema delta, the route delta, the enum delta), and workers only fill leaf BODIES — they never touch shared surfaces at all. **Why better:** Deletes a whole aspect by absorbing it into one that must exist anyway. If the contract is the single source of truth for the schema/route delta, then 'two leaves both add a column' is impossible — the column was decided once, at the top, before either leaf existed.
- **Invert the architecture: the shared singletons ARE the spine, built serially; parallelism is the exception** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Flip the seed's 'more processes = more power, the lock is a regrettable tax'. The shared singletons (migration sequence, barrel, enums, package.json) are the SPINE and are built by exactly ONE privileged serial worker; the parallel leaves merely request edits from it. Serialization of the spine IS the architecture; parallelism is the exception granted only to provably-independent leaves. **Why better:** A per-resource lease assumes symmetric peers fighting over a resource. But these surfaces aren't symmetric — they're a global namespace. Making the spine a single owning process eliminates the entire race class by construction and turns 'who holds the lock' into 'who do you ask' — simpler, auditable, and impossible to bypass.
- **Model every shared singleton as a CRDT — stitch is a merge, not a textual diff** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Model the schema barrel, route manifest, enum sets, barrel exports, and config maps (package.json deps, Tailwind theme keys, feature flags) as conflict-free replicated data types: a grow-only set/map of table/column/route/export/dep entries keyed by stable id. Each worktree mutates its own replica; stitch is a CRDT merge guaranteed to converge regardless of order or concurrency. The factory ships a typed merge function per config kind, not git's positional line-based three-way merge. **Why better:** git's line diff treats 'add dep lodash@4' and 'add dep zod@4' — or 'leaf A adds column foo' and 'leaf B adds column bar' — as conflicts even though they commute. CRDT semantics GUARANTEE clean convergence where git GAMBLES. The holy grail the seed wants ('more processes = more power') actually holds for the shared surfaces too, not just the independent ones, with zero coordination.
- **The build is one ACID transaction with per-surface savepoints, dialable isolation, and 2PC at the stitch** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Treat the whole swarm run as one ACID transaction over the shared singletons, with isolation dialed PER RESOURCE: serializable for schema/migration/enum, read-committed for independent leaf files. Each leaf's singleton-write is a savepoint. The green wave doesn't merge leaves one-by-one — at each contention boundary it runs two-phase commit: a PREPARE phase where every worker that touched a shared surface submits its proposed patch + lease token + the pre-image it edited against; the coordinator checks all pre-images still match HEAD; only then COMMITs the batch atomically, otherwise it aborts ONLY the conflicting leaf and re-dispatches it against the new state. **Why better:** The current factory has no notion of atomicity: a half-stitched run can leave schema.ts referencing a column the migration never created, and a stale pre-image silently corrupts the schema. Borrowing transaction + 2PC semantics gives all-or-nothing consistency, lets you DIAL strictness per resource instead of one blunt worktree-isolation assumption, and turns conflicts into a clean, cheap, targeted re-dispatch of one leaf instead of a poisoned merge that fails the whole green wave.
- **Singletons are BUILD ARTIFACTS, codegen'd from fragments — never hand-edited, like a lockfile** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — The shared files are no longer authored at all. Each leaf drops a fragment into its own folder (its slice of the enum, its one export line, its route entry, its table file); a deterministic codegen step at stitch concatenates all fragments into the barrel/enum/route-manifest/schema. No leaf ever edits a shared file, so there is no shared file to collide on — the file is owned by the TOOL, like a Bazel BUILD output or a lockfile that two humans never hand-edit. **Why better:** Removes the contention surface entirely rather than locking it. Barrel/enum/manifest merge conflicts — the single most common multi-agent collision — simply cease to exist, because a generated file has exactly one writer (the generator) by definition.
- **The singletons don't exist during the build — they are PROJECTED from leaf-local declarations at stitch** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Forbid every leaf from touching src/db/schema.ts, the migration dir, the route manifest, the Tailwind config, or any barrel. Those shared singletons DO NOT EXIST as writable files during the build — they are DERIVED at stitch time by projecting each leaf's local, self-contained declaration (its column intents, its route claim, its theme tokens, its exports) into the global file. Workers emit ONLY a typed CONTRIBUTION record ('+column orders.refund_at timestamptz') into an append-only intent log; a single deterministic reducer folds the log into the file. The factory generates the singletons; humans/leaves never edit them. **Why better:** You can't have a write-contention problem on a file nobody is allowed to write — it dissolves the lock question instead of answering it. Two leaves both 'adding a column' become two independent contribution records the projector merges deterministically; the residual collision surfaces as a conflict in the PROJECTION, caught mechanically, never as a silent stitch-time clobber. It's the same trick git itself uses: commits are appends to an intent log, the working tree is derived — N-way write contention on a monolith becomes N independent appends plus one mechanical fold.

### Contract renegotiation when a leaf proves the frozen spec wrong

_Current assumption: Contracts are 'frozen TOP-DOWN' before the swarm builds, and the assumption is they stay frozen — the build is a pure fill-in-the-blanks against an immutable signature/schema/test set. Unstated: leaf-level reality routinely DISPROVES the parent's contract (the API can't actually return that shape, the column type is wrong, the test encodes an impossible invariant, two sibling contracts are mutually inconsistent). There is no defined PROTOCOL for a worker to push a contract amendment back UP the tree, no arbiter for whether the fix is local or requires re-freezing siblings, and no propagation of an amended contract to already-built neighbors. A frozen contract that's wrong is worse than no contract — it forces N workers to build to a lie._

**Boldest reframe:** Bidirectional contracts: reality writes back up the tree automatically — the parent contract is a live view of its children's as-built reality, not a frozen prophecy, so "the spec is wrong" becomes impossible by construction (the contract can never disagree with reality because reality authors it; the architect's intent survives only as a divergence diff).

- **Contract Amendment Request as a first-class artifact (the CAR)** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — When a worker finds the frozen spec is wrong, it doesn't silently deviate or hack around it — it emits a structured Contract Amendment Request: the contract node it's challenging, the concrete evidence (the failing call, the actual API shape, the wrong column type), the minimal proposed delta, and a blast-radius guess (just me / my siblings / re-freeze the parent). The worker then PAUSES that leaf and picks up other ready work instead of building to a known lie. **Why better:** Today a wrong contract forces N workers to build to a lie or silently fork the truth. A typed CAR turns 'the spec is wrong' from an off-protocol panic into a normal, routable event the orchestrator already knows how to handle, and the evidence requirement stops workers amending contracts just because they're inconvenient.
- **Severity tiers that decide local-fix vs. re-freeze without a human** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Classify every amendment by blast radius: GREEN (purely internal to the leaf — worker just fixes it and notes it), YELLOW (changes the leaf's own outward signature — pauses only direct consumers), RED (changes shared schema or an invariant siblings depend on — escalates to the architect for a re-freeze). The router applies the cheapest tier that's defensible. **Why better:** The current model has no arbiter, so EITHER everything halts the swarm OR workers self-amend chaotically. A three-tier ladder gives ~80% of amendments (the GREEN ones) a zero-coordination path while reserving expensive top-down re-freezes for genuinely cross-cutting cases — matching coordination cost to actual blast radius.
- **Contract version stamps + a stale-neighbor sweep** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Every frozen contract carries a monotonic version. When an amendment lands, the contract bumps and every already-built node that consumed the old version is mechanically flagged STALE in the manifest. The green-wave stitch refuses to climb past a stale node until it's rebuilt or re-verified against the new version. **Why better:** Right now an amended contract silently leaves already-built neighbors built against the OLD shape — they look green but are broken at the seam. Version stamps make 'who is now out of date' a query instead of a discovery-at-integration-time disaster, and gate the stitch on consistency rather than mere local completion.
- **The arbiter is whoever froze it (escalate to the node's author, not a global judge)** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — An amendment escalates to exactly the agent that authored the parent contract — the Claude architect node one level up that wrote that signature/schema. It re-judges with the leaf's evidence in hand, then either accepts the delta (and propagates), counters with a different fix that preserves siblings, or rejects with a reason the leaf must build around. **Why better:** There's currently no defined arbiter at all. Routing the decision to the contract's own author keeps authority local to where the contract knowledge lives, avoids inventing a separate global tribunal, and naturally bounds how far up the tree any single amendment can travel.
- **Pre-freeze smoke-probe: verify external reality before the swarm spends** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Before freezing a contract that asserts an external reality (this API returns this shape, this column is this type, this library exposes this method), run one cheap probe — a real call, a schema introspection, a type-check against the actual dependency — and only freeze if the probe agrees. Probes run in the cheap scope-preview gate, before the swarm is dispatched. **Why better:** The cheapest amendment is the one you never need. Most contract-disproofs are knowable up front (the API genuinely can't return that shape) — catching them at freeze time for the price of one probe is vastly cheaper than discovering them across N parallel workers mid-run and unwinding their work.
- **Sibling-consistency cross-check at freeze time (contract type-checker over the cut)** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Before freezing a set of sibling contracts under a parent — or before the scope gate releases the swarm — run a mechanical consistency pass across the whole frozen layer: every producer/consumer pair must unify (shared types, units like cents-vs-dollars, nullability, error shapes, shared enums/IDs), and each failing test must reference a symbol some sibling actually provides. Mutually inconsistent siblings are rejected back to the architect before any worker starts. **Why better:** The hypothesis explicitly admits mutually-inconsistent siblings as a failure mode but only discovers it when a leaf hits it. A freeze-time/compile-time cross-check catches the contradiction at $0 (static check) while it's cheap to fix in one place, instead of letting two workers build incompatible halves of a seam that can never stitch.
- **Amendment ledger / immune registry that vaccinates future freezes** `small/rash` _(curated)_ — Every accepted amendment is logged with its trigger (what reality disproved the spec) as an antigen→antibody pair in graphify's shared knowledge graph (e.g. 'Supabase REST returns snake_case', 'this provider never returns nested arrays', 'this column must be bigint not int'). The architect queries this immune memory at freeze time, so a contradiction proven once by any leaf — this run OR future runs — becomes a freeze-time lint rule and is never frozen-wrong again. **Why better:** Without memory the factory re-learns the same contract lies every run. An adaptive-immunity ledger turns each painful amendment into a permanent vaccine, so the freeze step gets monotonically smarter and the amendment rate trends down over the project's life — compounding the current frozen-and-forget model can't deliver. graphify already exists as the shared graph; this gives it a defensive memory.
- **Provisional vs. load-bearing grades: freeze the seam, mark the guesses THAW-able** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Distinguish two grades at freeze time. LOAD-BEARING parts (public signature, shared schema, the seam other nodes depend on) are truly frozen; internal/uncertain assertions are explicitly marked PROVISIONAL. A worker may revise a PROVISIONAL part unilaterally with just a logged note; touching a LOAD-BEARING part requires the full amendment escalation. **Why better:** The flat 'everything is frozen' rule forces the heavy renegotiation protocol even for trivial internal guesses, throttling parallelism. Grading the contract concentrates the expensive ceremony on the few parts that actually bind neighbors — a wrong-but-internal guess no longer triggers a tree-wide event.
- **Contracts carry a confidence score and decay rate, not a binary freeze stamp** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Every contract FIELD carries a confidence score and a decay rate. High-confidence fields (a UUID PK) freeze hard; low-confidence fields (an external API's response shape the architect GUESSED) ship as provisional and any leaf that touches reality is authorized to overwrite them without escalation. The freeze isn't binary — it's a gradient the architect annotates at emit time, at field granularity rather than node granularity. **Why better:** Most contract-vs-reality collisions happen on exactly the fields the architect was least sure about. Pre-marking those at field-level confidence removes the renegotiation ceremony for ~80% of cases — the worker just corrects the guess and moves on, no arbiter needed — while still hard-freezing the structurally certain parts.
- **Quarantine-and-continue: a disproven leaf must not stall its independent siblings** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — When a leaf opens a RED amendment, the orchestrator quarantines only the subtree that genuinely depends on the contested contract and lets every independent lane keep building. The quarantined work parks at its last green state with a resume token, so when the amendment resolves it rebuilds just the affected nodes, not the whole branch. **Why better:** The unstated assumption is that a wrong contract blocks the build, but blocking the WHOLE swarm on one bad contract wastes the parallelism that is the factory's entire advantage. Scoping the freeze to the true dependency cone keeps throughput high while renegotiation happens, instead of idling the worktrees.
- **Contracts as falsifiable hypotheses with a market for disproof** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Reframe every frozen contract not as a law but as a scientific hypothesis the swarm is PAID to try to break. Each worker reaching a leaf is rewarded (in a budget/priority economy) for producing a counterexample that disproves its parent's contract — a payload the API physically can't return, a column type that loses precision, a test encoding an impossible invariant. The strongest disproof auto-triggers renegotiation; contracts that survive sustained adversarial assault earn a 'hardened' badge and propagate faster. **Why better:** The current model has no incentive to find the lie and every incentive to build to it. Inverting the reward so workers HUNT for contract-breaking evidence converts the silent failure mode (build N things to a wrong spec) into the explicit success mode (the swarm self-corrects before spending).
- **The Renegotiation Court: a standing dual-model tribunal with precedent** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — A persistent Claude/Codex tribunal sits above the tree on an amendment queue. When a worker files an amendment it argues a case: Codex (the builder who hit reality) is prosecution, Claude (the architect who froze the spec) is defense, a third judge model rules LOCAL fix / SIBLING re-freeze / DISMISS. The ruling is a signed, appealable artifact with precedent, so the same class of conflict resolves the same way next time, and the amended contract gets a new version the stitch keys off. **Why better:** Today there is literally no arbiter for 'is this fix local or does it require re-freezing siblings?' — the single hardest question in the aspect. A standing court with precedent turns ad-hoc panic into a deterministic, auditable, learning institution with one consistent blast-radius policy instead of N workers each guessing.
- **Speculative multiverse: fork the subtree on amendment and let realities race** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — When a leaf disproves a contract, don't pause to renegotiate — instantly fork the affected subtree into parallel git-worktree universes: one keeps the old contract, one adopts the amendment, optionally one tries a synthesis. The swarm builds ALL of them concurrently; the universe whose green-wave reaches the root first and cleanest wins and is merged, the losers are garbage-collected. **Why better:** Renegotiation as currently imagined is a STALL — workers wait on an up-tree decision. Speculative forking makes amendment FREE in wall-clock time and resolves it with evidence (which branch is green) instead of an upfront ruling that could itself be wrong: more processes literally buy you the answer to 'which contract was right.'
- **Contracts that carry their own renegotiation protocol (self-amending clauses)** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Every frozen contract ships with an embedded amendment grammar — pre-declared 'give' joints: this field's type is negotiable within these bounds; this endpoint may add but never remove keys; this test's threshold may relax to X. A worker hitting reality consults the contract's OWN rules to decide whether its fix is in-bounds (auto-apply, no up-tree trip) or out-of-bounds (escalate). The architect designs the negotiation surface at freeze time, not just the shape. **Why better:** The unstated gap is that 'frozen' is binary — fully rigid or fully open. Pre-declaring WHERE a contract may flex lets ~90% of leaf-level corrections resolve locally and instantly, reserving expensive up-tree renegotiation only for genuinely structural surprises.
- **Blast-radius simulation: render and cost the ripple before the amendment lands** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Before any contract change commits, a graphify-powered impact engine simulates the amendment against the WHOLE contract graph and renders the literal blast radius in the cockpit — these 3 siblings break, these 7 already-built leaves need patching, this test invariant becomes satisfiable, total re-build cost is N tokens. The amendment can be accepted, rejected, or auto-narrowed to minimize blast radius before a single worker is re-dispatched. **Why better:** Current design has NO propagation of an amended contract to already-built neighbors — they silently drift out of sync. Making the ripple visible and costed turns invisible cross-leaf corruption into a deliberate, bounded, previewed decision.
- **Bidirectional contracts: reality writes back up the tree automatically** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Contracts become two-way bindings, not top-down decrees. The instant a leaf's real implementation settles on a concrete shape (the API genuinely returns THIS), that as-built truth flows UP and rewrites the parent contract by default — the parent is a live view of its children's reality, not a frozen prophecy. The architect's original spec is demoted to a 'desired intent' annotation that the build either honors or visibly diverges from. graphify (the as-built graph) becomes the binding contract. **Why better:** It dissolves the whole 'a frozen contract that's wrong is worse than no contract' problem by making 'wrong' impossible — the contract can never disagree with reality because reality authors it. The architect's intent survives as a diff signal ('you wanted X, the build gave Y') rather than a lie everyone builds toward.
- **A learned 'contract smell' / fragility model that pre-disproves risky specs** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Train a judge on the history of every amendment this factory has filed — every time a frozen contract was later proven wrong, and why. At freeze time it scores each contract for fragility ('this shape historically gets renegotiated 70% of the time at the persistence boundary') and forces a cheap single-leaf SPIKE on only the riskiest contracts BEFORE the full swarm commits, catching the lie with one worker instead of N. **Why better:** The current scope-preview gate checks COST but never CONTRACT TRUTHFULNESS. A learned fragility prior moves disproof from mid-build (expensive, N workers wasted) to pre-build (one targeted spike on the worst offenders), and the factory gets smarter at freezing contracts the more it runs.
- **Inconsistent siblings auto-spawn a reconciling adapter node (self-healing tree)** `small/rash` _(curated)_ — When two sibling leaves prove their contracts can't both be true (one needs UTC, the other local; one returns a list, the other a map; one cents, one dollars), the conflict itself becomes a first-class node: the tree GROWS a new reconciliation/adapter node between the siblings and the parent, with its own contract (a thin translation shim), dispatched to a worker. Inconsistency is resolved by ADDING structure at the one seam, not by forcing one sibling to lose or rebuilding either. **Why better:** Today sibling-vs-sibling contradiction has no defined resolution — someone manually picks a winner and re-freezes (O(N) edits, regression risk). An adapter is O(1) additive code at exactly one seam, touches nothing already-built, parallelizes trivially, and preserves both siblings' hard-won leaf reality — which is how real microservice/module boundaries survive independent teams.
- **Probe leaves run FIRST; the parent contract is synthesized from their ground-truth** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Contracts are authored at the moment of MAXIMUM ignorance because authoring is conflated with top-down decomposition. Decouple them: split each node into a cheap 'probe' leaf (curl the real API, introspect the real table, run one query, write the one hard test) that executes BEFORE its siblings, and synthesize the parent's contract FROM probe returns rather than from the architect's imagination. The contract is born a measurement, not a prediction. **Why better:** You can't be 'disproven by a leaf' if the leaf that establishes ground truth ran first and the contract is its output. This kills the entire renegotiation class for anything observable — converting contracts from predictions into measurements before the swarm spends a dollar.
- **Contracts are bids the leaf can ACCEPT / COUNTER / REJECT, not laws it must obey** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — A contract is the parent's BID for what a leaf should expose, not a decree. The leaf — which has LOCAL ground truth the architect structurally lacks — can ACCEPT, COUNTER (propose an amended signature with a one-line reason), or REJECT. A counter auto-propagates up unless a sibling's already-accepted contract conflicts, which is the ONLY thing that triggers the arbiter. **Why better:** Inverts the default from 'comply or escalate' to 'correct silently unless you'd break a sibling.' The arbiter fires only on real cross-leaf conflict, not on every honest correction — most amendments cost zero coordination.
- **Collapse the contract to ONE canonical test; signature + schema are generated projections** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — We freeze signature AND schema AND tests as three artifacts that can disagree (a test can encode an impossible invariant the signature permits). Collapse the contract to ONE canonical artifact — the executable test/property — and treat signature + schema as generated PROJECTIONS of it. A leaf can't 'disprove the signature against the test' because there's one source; when reality breaks the test you amend the one canonical thing and the projections regenerate. **Why better:** Eliminates intra-contract inconsistency (the 'test encodes an impossible invariant' failure mode) by construction — there's nothing for the three artifacts to disagree about. One amend point, deterministically propagated.
- **Contracts version like a schema migration: neighbors get a codemod diff-patch, not a rebuild** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Every contract change emits a semantic DIFF (field added / type widened / field renamed) and a generated codemod. Already-built neighbors receive the codemod plus a targeted re-test of ONLY the touched surface — a green ripple, not a green-wave restart. Amendment cost is proportional to the change, not to subtree size. **Why better:** 'Wrong frozen contract forces N rebuilds' becomes 'N tiny auto-patches + scoped re-tests' — cheap enough that the system stops fearing amendment and over-freezing to avoid it, because most amendments touch one field, not the whole contract.
- **Contract amendment as a reverse-dependency PR up the tree (Bazel/Nx affected-targets)** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — When a leaf proves its parent contract wrong, the worker opens a typed 'contract amendment PR' against the parent node. The orchestrator computes the contract's reverse-dependency set — exactly like Bazel/Nx compute affected targets from a changed BUILD file — and re-runs ONLY the impacted sibling leaves against the amended spec, leaving the rest of the green wave untouched. **Why better:** The current model has zero propagation: an amended contract silently diverges from N neighbors built to the old lie. Reverse-dependency analysis is exactly what build systems exist for — it makes the blast radius computable instead of unknown, so you rebuild the 3 affected leaves, not all 40 or none.
- **Saga compensation: a wrong contract triggers automatic rollback of poisoned siblings (Temporal)** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Treat each frozen contract as a saga step with a registered compensation. When a leaf disproves the contract, the orchestrator fires the compensation for every sibling built against the old version — reverting their worktrees to pre-build state and re-queuing them — rather than leaving half-built-to-a-lie artifacts in the tree. **Why better:** Today a disproved contract is discovered AFTER siblings have committed work to it, with no undo. Workflow engines solved exactly this — a failed step doesn't corrupt the system, it triggers ordered compensation. It converts 'a wrong contract is worse than no contract' into 'a wrong contract self-heals by un-building its victims.'
- **Consumer-driven contract tests: the consumers' test suite IS the arbiter (Pact)** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Every contract is versioned, and each consuming sibling registers a consumer-driven contract test asserting what IT actually needs from the contract. A producing leaf can only amend the contract if the amendment still passes all registered consumer tests; if it breaks one, the amendment is rejected at the producer and escalated to an arbiter. **Why better:** The 'frozen' assumption treats the contract as the producer's truth, but its real owners are its CONSUMERS. Consumer-driven contracts make 'is this fix local or does it require re-freezing siblings?' a mechanical test result instead of a judgment call — the test suite IS the arbiter.
- **Andon cord: any leaf can stop the line and pull a contract to the architect (Toyota TPS)** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Give every worker a literal andon cord — a single primitive that HALTS dispatch of new leaves under the affected subtree and surfaces the disproved contract to the Claude-architect tier for re-judgment. The swarm doesn't keep spending tokens building toward a known-bad spec; it stops, the architect re-freezes, the line restarts. **Why better:** Right now there's no STOP — workers keep building to the lie because nothing pauses the swarm. Toyota's insight is that running the line on a known defect is the most expensive thing you can do. A cheap stop-the-subtree primitive prevents the factory from spending its $200+$100 quota manufacturing scrap.
- **Editorial conform / change-order: amendments flow through a reconcile pass (VFX pipeline)** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Borrow the VFX 'conform' stage — the contract graph is an edit decision list, and when a shot (leaf) comes back proving a plate (spec) wrong, it doesn't mutate the master; it files a versioned change-order that a dedicated conform pass reconciles against the master and re-publishes downstream. Workers always pull the latest conformed contract version before building, never a stale freeze. **Why better:** VFX pipelines run hundreds of artists against constantly-changing shared specs and survive via versioned publishes + a conform/reconcile gate, never by freezing. This replaces 'frozen forever' with 'frozen-per-version with a reconcile step,' so an amendment can't silently desync a neighbor — the neighbor re-pulls and sees it.
- **Two-phase commit on the freeze: leaf feasibility probes are the PREPARE phase** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Before a contract is hard-frozen, dispatch ultra-cheap 'feasibility probe' workers to EACH leaf that just answer 'can you actually satisfy this signature/schema/test?' That's the PREPARE phase; the contract only COMMITS to frozen once every leaf votes yes. A no-vote forces renegotiation BEFORE the expensive parallel build spends a dollar. **Why better:** The current model freezes optimistically and discovers infeasibility only after the swarm has built against it. Distributed-DB two-phase commit moves contradiction-detection BEFORE the spend — most 'the API can't return that / the column type is wrong / two siblings are inconsistent' failures are caught in a cheap prepare round instead of an expensive full build.
- **Don't freeze contracts — freeze only the behavioral TEST, let signatures float** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Delete the 'frozen signature + frozen schema' half of the contract. The only thing frozen top-down is the BEHAVIORAL test (the observable invariant: 'given this offer, the war-room pipeline shows N stages'). Signatures, shapes, and column types are emergent — workers negotiate them peer-to-peer at the seam, and the green test is the sole arbiter. There is nothing to renegotiate up the tree because the parent never asserted a shape. **Why better:** A renegotiation protocol is overhead that only exists because you over-specified. If the parent freezes WHAT must be true and never HOW, then 'the API can't return that shape' isn't a contract violation — it's just a worker choosing a different shape that still passes the test. You delete the entire arbiter/propagation machinery by never creating the conflict.
- **There is no 'up' — contracts are published UP from built leaves, not inherited down** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Invert the direction of authority. Contracts are not handed DOWN from parent to leaf; they are PUBLISHED UP to a shared registry the instant a leaf is built and green. The plan-tree is a dispatch hint, not a source of truth. A sibling reads its neighbor's actual, as-built, published contract — never the parent's prediction of it. **Why better:** The premise 'leaf reality disproves the parent's contract' assumes the parent's contract is authoritative. If it never was — if the parent only emitted a guess and the real contract is whatever the leaf shipped — then 'disproving' is impossible by construction. graphify already IS the as-built graph; make THAT the contract and stop pretending the top-down prediction is binding.
- **A wrong frozen contract HALTS the subtree and triggers a fresh re-plan (no surgical amendment)** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Refuse to build a renegotiation protocol. When a leaf proves its parent contract impossible, the worker does not amend, propagate, or arbitrate — it raises a hard STOP that invalidates the entire subtree and bounces the whole branch back to the Claude architect for a fresh re-plan from that node. No surgical amendment, no patching neighbors. Re-plan is cheaper and more correct than reconciliation. **Why better:** Surgical amendment-with-propagation is the single hardest distributed-systems problem you could pick (consistent partial re-freeze across N in-flight workers). A wrong contract usually means the architect mis-decomposed, not that one column type is off. Re-planning a subtree is a 5-minute Claude call; a correct live-renegotiation arbiter is a research project that will be subtly wrong forever.
- **Frozen-but-wrong is the FEATURE: build to the lie, let the stitch fail loudly in one place** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Do the opposite of renegotiating. Force every worker to build EXACTLY to the frozen contract even when the leaf knows it's wrong — and make the mechanical stitch (the green wave) the ONLY place wrongness surfaces, as a loud, located, batch failure. No mid-build back-pressure at all. The stitch produces a precise diff of every contract the build disproved, which the architect re-freezes in one synchronous pass. **Why better:** A renegotiation protocol smears decision-making across N workers mid-flight, creating races and inconsistent partial states. Concentrating ALL contract-reality conflicts into one deterministic checkpoint trades a little wasted leaf-work for total observability and zero concurrency hazard. One architect re-freeze pass over a complete conflict-list beats N uncoordinated amendments — 'worse than no contract' is false if the lie fails fast and in one place.
- **Delete sibling-consistency as a goal — every seam is an adapter, never a shared truth** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — The 'two sibling contracts are mutually inconsistent → propagate the amendment' problem only exists because siblings are forced to agree. Invert it: siblings are NEVER required to be consistent. Every cross-leaf boundary gets a thin generated adapter/translation shim. When contracts disagree you don't reconcile them — you generate a shim between them. **Why better:** Reconciliation-and-propagation is O(N) edits across already-built code with regression risk. Adapters are O(1) additive code at exactly one seam, touch nothing already-built, and parallelize trivially. The aspect assumes inconsistency must be resolved upward; an adapter says inconsistency is fine if it's bridged locally — how real module boundaries survive independent teams.
- **Kill the contract layer for cheap leaves; only freeze contracts at expensive high-fan-in seams** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Reject the assumption that everything gets a frozen contract. Most leaves are cheap enough to one-shot AND cheap enough to re-roll — they get NO contract, just a test. Freezing (and therefore any renegotiation machinery) is reserved for a tiny set of expensive, high-fan-in seams (the DB schema, a public API boundary). Renegotiation isn't a tree-wide protocol; it's a rare manual event at 3-4 nodes a HUMAN reviews. **Why better:** A uniform contract-everywhere policy creates the N-workers-built-to-a-lie failure mode. If 95% of leaves never had a binding contract, 95% of contract-falsifications can't happen, and the remaining 5% are so few and so important that a human reviews them — replacing a speculative automated arbiter with the correct amount of attention exactly where it's load-bearing.
- **Invert who's wrong: a falsified contract fails the LEAF until proven otherwise (evidence-gated)** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Flip the default verdict. When a leaf and its contract disagree, the presumption is the WORKER hallucinated, not that the contract is wrong. The leaf must produce hard, graphify-verifiable evidence (a real API response capture, a real failing migration) before any contract can even be questioned. No evidence → the leaf is rejected and re-dispatched, contract untouched. Only evidence-backed falsifications reach an architect. **Why better:** An open renegotiation protocol is a denial-of-service vector: every confused worker 'proves the spec wrong' and floods the arbiter, eroding the contract's value to zero. Defaulting to 'the contract stands, prove otherwise' preserves the contract's authority (its whole point) while still letting GENUINE reality-conflicts through — gated by evidence the graphify layer can verify.

### Reproducibility, provenance & the same-intent-twice problem

_Current assumption: Implicitly each run is a one-way street: intent in, artifact out, done. Unstated: LLM builds are NON-deterministic, so the same intent run twice yields different artifacts, and there is no captured RUN MANIFEST (model versions, prompts, seeds, tool versions, golden-template hash, which worker built which leaf) that makes a build replayable, auditable, or diffable. Without provenance you cannot answer 'why did this leaf come out this way', cannot re-run a single failed leaf deterministically, cannot bisect a regression to a worker decision, and cannot trust that re-running the factory on an unchanged subtree won't silently rewrite working code._

**Boldest reframe:** The Build Manifest is the real artifact; code is a cache — invert the factory's source of truth so the signed, content-addressed manifest is canonical and the code on disk is a rebuildable, derived projection of it. This is the boldest because it doesn't add provenance, it relocates the center of gravity of the whole system: once the manifest (not the code) is what you ship and trust, replay, diff, audit, selective re-run, and content-addressed caching all stop being features to build and become trivial reads of the canonical object — and it carries the Deterministic Twin's logical endpoint (freeze the model into the manifest) and the Notarized Build's external attestation as natural consequences.

- **Per-leaf run-card sidecar file** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Every leaf the swarm builds drops a tiny `<leaf>.runcard.json` next to (or in a parallel `.factory/` tree mirroring) its artifact, capturing model id+version, the exact prompt+system, temperature/seed, tool versions, golden-template hash, worktree commit, and which worker process built it. The artifact and its provenance ship together and travel with git. **Why better:** Turns the invisible, lost build context into a durable, greppable record so you can finally answer 'why did this leaf come out this way' and re-run exactly one leaf instead of the whole tree.
- **Content-hash the inputs, not the outputs (cache hit = skip rebuild)** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Compute a deterministic `input_hash` for each leaf from its frozen contract (signature + schema slice + failing tests + golden-template hash + relevant graph subset + pinned model id). Store it in the run-card; on re-run, if the input_hash is unchanged the factory SKIPS rebuilding and reuses the existing artifact. This is the local, per-leaf version of a content-addressed cache. **Why better:** Directly kills the 'silently rewrites working code' failure: an unchanged subtree is provably unchanged and never gets a non-deterministic redo, making re-runs cheap, safe, and trustworthy.
- **Replay mode: pin the manifest, re-dispatch one node** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — A `factory replay <leaf>` command reads that leaf's run-card and re-dispatches the SAME worker type with the SAME pinned model/version/prompt/seed and the SAME contract, ignoring any drifted global config. Output goes to a scratch worktree for diffing against the original. **Why better:** Converts 'each run is a one-way street' into a deterministic-as-possible replay, so a failed leaf can be re-attempted under identical conditions rather than re-rolling the entire build and hoping.
- **Build-diff view in the Cockpit (manifest delta -> artifact delta)** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — When the same intent (or subtree) is run twice, the Cockpit renders a node-by-node three-way diff: which leaves changed, and for each changed leaf, which provenance/input field differed (model version bumped? prompt edited? template hash moved? seed? resolved context?) aligned with the output file diff. Unchanged leaves render grey/collapsed, and an output that changed with ZERO input change is flagged as pure non-determinism to investigate. **Why better:** Makes the same-intent-twice problem visible and explainable instead of a mysterious wall of changed files — you immediately see whether a diff came from a real intent change or just model nondeterminism, and you can trust the factory enough to run it more than once.
- **Seed everything that accepts a seed** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Thread a single run-level `--seed` (and per-leaf derived seeds, e.g. `hash(run_seed, leaf_path)`) into every generation call that supports it — model sampling, any randomized template choice, ordering of parallel dispatch. Record the seed in the manifest. **Why better:** Squeezes out the controllable slice of nondeterminism so replays land far closer to byte-identical, and the run-level seed becomes a single knob to reproduce or deliberately re-roll a whole build.
- **Pin-and-warn on model/tool drift at the scope gate** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — The manifest pins exact model ids+versions and key tool versions at run start. On any subsequent run, the factory compares live versions to the pinned set and surfaces a one-line banner ('opus bumped 4.8->4.9; codex CLI 1.2->1.3 since last run — replays may diverge') before the swarm spends. **Why better:** Provenance isn't just for autopsies — proactively warning that the substrate moved explains future divergence in advance and lets you choose to pin-back, turning silent drift into an informed decision at the scope gate.
- **The Provenance Hologram: keystroke-level reverse traceability** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Render every shipped artifact as a fully reverse-traceable hologram in the Cockpit: click any character of generated code (or any file/asset/section) and it lights up the entire causal cone behind it — the prompt, the seed, the parent contract, the failing test that constrained it, the sibling leaves it had to integrate with, the model and the exact decode that produced it. Provenance is also baked invisibly into each artifact (comment header for code, EXIF/sidecar for art, frontmatter for docs) so the backpointer travels with the file. **Why better:** Answers 'why did this come out this way' instantly and visually instead of never. Provenance stops being metadata in a log and becomes a property of the artifact you can interrogate at the keystroke level, extending the project's 'every claim carries its support' Evidence-Bundle discipline down to the factory's own outputs.
- **Counterfactual forking: re-run one leaf 100 ways, keep the winner's manifest** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Because every leaf is independently addressed and contract-isolated, re-fire just ONE failed leaf across 100 seeds/prompts/models in parallel, auto-judge against its frozen failing tests, and promote the winner — while recording the manifest of all 100 attempts. You get deterministic targeted re-runs AND a provenance trail of the roads not taken, AND a best-of-N quality lift over a single replayable run. **Why better:** Today a failed leaf forces re-rolling whole subtrees non-deterministically. This makes 'deterministically re-run a single failed leaf' real, captures WHY the chosen output won over its 99 rivals, and turns non-determinism from a defect into a quality engine.
- **Frozen-Determinism Mode: ban regeneration inside a locked subtree** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Mark any subtree 'FROZEN'. Inside it, the factory physically cannot regenerate — it may only replay from cassette or refuse. To change a frozen leaf you must explicitly thaw it, which forces a new manifest, a diff, and a human gate. Working code becomes structurally immune to silent rewrites; stability is the default and regeneration is the explicit, audited exception. **Why better:** Directly slays the worst failure mode — 'will re-running the factory silently rewrite my working code?' — by making it impossible by default, inverting the current implicit assumption that every run regenerates everything.
- **Twin-run divergence as a first-class quality signal (divergence heatmap)** `small/rash` _(curated)_ — Deliberately run high-stakes subtrees TWICE with different seeds/workers and diff the two artifacts. Convergence (both agree) is a confidence signal you can ship on; divergence localizes exactly which leaves are under-specified. Surface a 'divergence heatmap' in the cockpit over the plan-tree. **Why better:** Reframes non-determinism as free entropy you can measure: two runs disagreeing isn't a bug to suppress, it's the cheapest possible detector of an ambiguous contract — turning the very flaw (irreproducibility) into the QA mechanism.
- **The andon cord for non-reproducible leaves: stop the line on divergence** `small/rash` _(curated)_ — Toyota's andon cord lets any station halt the whole line on a defect. Adapt it as an auto-gate: before a leaf's artifact feeds the green-wave stitch, the factory builds it TWICE (or N times) at fixed inputs and checks convergence. If the builds disagree beyond a threshold, the leaf pulls the cord — it blocks its own promotion and escalates to the cockpit instead of letting a coin-flip artifact propagate up the tree. **Why better:** Catches non-reproducibility at the exact node where it's born, before it's stitched into dependents and becomes expensive to unwind — the current flow has no convergence check, so an unstable leaf gets built ON TOP OF and the instability compounds silently up the whole tree.
- **The lot-traceability stamp: serial numbers + recall-by-lot** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Borrow manufacturing lot/serial traceability — stamp every file (or sidecar) with a provenance ID resolving to which worker built it, from which contract version, which model+prompt+template-hash, in which run, at what altitude tier. A recall ('this golden template was poisoned') becomes a query: find every artifact in the field built from lot X, exactly like recalling every car with a bad airbag from a known production batch. **Why better:** Today there's no way to know WHICH leaves inherited a bad template or regressed prompt — you'd re-audit by hand. A serial number makes blast-radius a lookup instead of an investigation, and turns 'trust me it's fine' into an auditable chain of custody.
- **Golden-frame regression gate (VFX render-farm style)** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — VFX farms never trust a re-render — they diff the new frame against an approved 'golden frame' and flag drift before it ships. Adapt it: when a leaf is rebuilt, diff the new artifact against the last GREEN one for that contract. If they differ, the change doesn't auto-merge — it surfaces in the cockpit as flagged drift with before/after and the input delta that explains it. Identical output = silent pass. **Why better:** Turns non-determinism from an invisible risk into a visible, gated event: a re-run can no longer quietly replace working code — any divergence must be explained by an input change or accepted by a human.
- **Regression bisect over the run-tree (git-bisect for worker decisions)** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Model the plan-tree build as a DAG of hashed leaves with recorded build decisions in the same append-only event log ArtLab already uses (events.jsonl).
