The oracle is not a model-authored test — it is DIVERGENCE: feed both implementations the same generated inputs and any disagreement flags a bug in at least one, with no human-authored expected values needed. **Why better:** Sidesteps the authored-test problem entirely: ground truth becomes consensus between two minds that never spoke, not an assertion one mind made about itself. Two-wrong-in-the-same-way failures are far rarer than one model rubber-stamping its own work.
- **Two heterogeneous oracles must agree, or the disagreement IS the deliverable** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Require green from two lineage-independent oracles — the builder-family suite AND a from-scratch checker a different model derives directly off the human intent. Done requires both green; when they diverge, the divergence (not a forced pick) is surfaced to the human as the single highest-value output of the run. **Why better:** One suite proves self-consistency; two lineage-independent oracles agreeing proves something closer to truth because shared blind spots can't cancel both. Surfacing disagreement honors the 'never silently ship a disagreement' principle — making the oracle's uncertainty visible is more honest than a green wave that hides it.
- **Behavioral e2e leaf at the artifact altitude for app-class runs** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — For any T2/T3 run, require at least one Playwright-style e2e spec that drives the real running artifact through the user's headline 'north-star loop,' generated from the acceptance list and gated independently of unit tests. **Why better:** Unit-leaf green can be 100% while the assembled app is broken on wiring, routing, auth, or data plumbing. The Tower already ships north-star-loop.spec and new-user-activation-smoke.spec as exactly this artifact oracle; generating one per run guarantees green includes 'the thing actually runs and does the headline job,' not just 'the pieces self-agree.'
- **The Artifact Trial: put the assembled running thing on trial, not the tree** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — The top-of-tree gate is not aggregated leaf tests — it is the assembled artifact exercised as a human would. The built app is deployed to an ephemeral sandbox and driven by an agent acting as the user; a deck is rendered and read end-to-end; a decision is stress-tested against its own stated criteria. tower-ship-gate (tsc/lint/vitest/build/e2e/bans) becomes the FLOOR and 'a stranger uses the artifact and it does the job' becomes the CEILING. Leaf-green is necessary but never sufficient; only artifact acceptance closes the tree. (Steals the VFX final-shot review and Bazel's unit-vs-integration-target split: a film never ships because every department's internal QC passed — it ships when the supervisor signs off on the composited final frame.) **Why better:** Correctness is not compositional — every slide can pass and the deck still be incoherent; a thousand green dots never met each other. Moving the real oracle to the artifact level means the success signal measures the thing the user actually receives. The Tower literally already has this oracle in tower-ship-gate; this pulls it to the crown of the tree.
- **Canary the artifact: a live smoke run against the real thing, not the stub** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Before declaring done, actually RUN the artifact for real — boot the built app and drive a few true user journeys, execute the decision against live data, open the generated deck and check slides render — in an isolated sandbox, separate from the model-controlled stub/leaf tests. Green leaves get a candidate; the canary smoke run gets 'done.' (Steals progressive-delivery canary deploys; the Tower already runs an off-platform canary hitting real prod every 15m.) **Why better:** Leaf and integration tests run against stubs and mocks the model controls; a canary exercises composed, deployed reality the model cannot have pre-satisfied — the gap between 'every part passed in isolation' and 'the whole thing works' that every assembly line closes with a final functional test, not a parts inventory.
- **Reverse-Spec / Echo-back Oracle: re-derive intent from the as-built artifact and diff it** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — After the build, a fresh COLD agent with no memory of building it inspects the finished artifact and writes from scratch what it believes the thing DOES and what intent it serves. That reconstructed spec is semantically diffed against the original user ask at the root; a gap above threshold blocks and surfaces exactly where the build drifted — and the human confirms the echo, not the test count. (Steals manufacturing's coordinate-measuring-machine as-built-vs-as-designed inspection and extends graphify from 'matches contract' to 'matches PURPOSE.') **Why better:** Every test-based oracle answers 'does the code match the tests?' — none answers 'does it do what the human MEANT?' Re-deriving intent from the as-built artifact and diffing the original ask is a true ground-truth check on the intent gap, inserted at the one place it's cheap: a single confirm-or-correct on a plain-language restatement. Catches 'built the wrong thing correctly,' which no self-authored green can ever detect.
- **Golden-master snapshots from a frozen reference realization** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — At contract-freeze time the orchestrator generates a tiny reference realization of each subtree — a stub render, a sample output row, a rendered slide thumbnail — and freezes it as a golden master. As the swarm builds, every node's real output is diffed against its golden; drift beyond tolerance halts the green wave and surfaces a visual/structural diff in the cockpit, exactly like the byte-diff CI already protecting Otis/CEO art. (Steals VFX golden frames + Nx/Turborepo content-hashing.) **Why better:** Leaf tests check behavior the model imagined; golden masters check the artifact against a human-anchored reference captured at intent-freeze, catching the failure where every leaf is internally green but the COMPOSITION silently drifted from what was promised. The Tower's existing byte-diff workflow proves this oracle pattern works in practice.
- **Provenance-signed green: a test result is worthless without an audit trail** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — A leaf's 'green' is not a boolean but a signed record — which model authored the test, which different model wrote the code, the mutation score, whether the test ever ran RED before going green, and the diff that turned it green. Tests are also byte-protected the way Otis/CEO art is CI-frozen: write-once from above, read-only below — any worker that weakens, deletes, or rewrites a test to pass trips a guard and is rejected. The cockpit refuses to climb the green wave through any node whose green lacks valid provenance (e.g. a test 'born green' that never failed). (Steals Bazel remote-execution provenance + SLSA supply-chain attestation.) **Why better:** A test committed already-passing that never caught a red is indistinguishable from no test at all, and nothing today stops a struggling worker from loosening the very test blocking it — the fastest path to green is to lower the bar. Demanding a red-to-green transition and cross-model authorship as ATTESTED provenance, plus freezing the oracle, makes 'pass the test' the only legal route to green and turns an unfalsifiable claim into an auditable one.
- **Tower-ship-gate as the mandatory, and possibly SOLE, top-of-tree gate** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Promote tower-ship-gate (tsc --noEmit, lint, vitest, build, e2e, bans) from a manual 'before you claim done' habit to the factory's non-negotiable root gate — the green wave may not reach the root and declare the artifact done until ship-gate passes on the assembled whole. The aggressive variant: collapse the multi-level oracle to ONE — leaf nodes have no independent done-state at all; they are just material the stitch consumes, accepted or rejected wholesale by this single top gate. **Why better:** The Tower already HAS a battle-tested, stop-at-first-failure, pasted-output oracle the model can't fake (the app must actually build and boot). Wiring it as the literal top-of-tree gate closes the artifact-vs-leaf gap with zero new tooling; the collapse variant argues N weaker self-authored leaf gates add gameable surface for no truth, and one real top gate beats them.
- **Merge the oracle into graphify: done = reality matches the contract graph** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Fold ground-truth into graphify's as-built verification. The success signal is structural: does the built artifact's actual call graph, schema, and type signatures conform to the contract graph frozen top-down from intent before the build? Behavioral leaf tests become optional decoration. **Why better:** The contract graph was frozen top-down from intent before any code existed, so checking conformance to it is checking against an earlier, independent artifact. Tests authored DURING the build by the builder are downstream and circular — one graph-conformance oracle is harder to game than thousands of self-authored leaf assertions.
- **Stake the oracle: leaves carry a confidence bond the artifact gate can slash** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Each leaf declares a confidence and 'what would prove me wrong' when it self-reports green. If the artifact-level gate later fails and bisects the cause to that leaf, its green is retroactively voided and its test pattern is added to a growing blocklist of tautology signatures the factory refuses next time. **Why better:** Today a leaf's green is final and free — there's no downward pressure on test quality and no learning when self-consistency lied. A slashing/bond loop makes vacuous green COSTLY and turns each artifact-level failure into permanent immunity against that class of fake test, so the oracle sharpens over runs instead of repeating its blind spots.
- **Human spot-check gate on a sampled subtree, not every leaf** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — The cockpit surfaces ONE randomly-sampled green leaf per subtree — its diff, its tests, and the acceptance statement it claims to satisfy — for a ~10-second thumbs-up/down before the green wave propagates past that subtree. **Why better:** The factory is 'autonomous with oversight' but currently oversees only direction, never correctness. Sampling makes the human an actual ground-truth oracle at near-zero cost, catching 'green but wrong-meaning' leaves no model-authored test would flag — mirroring the approve-direction gate pattern the user already trusts, without reintroducing humans mid-run on every node.
- **Human acceptance gate as the tree's keystone** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Borrow ArtLab's two-human-gate pattern and make a single cheap human acceptance the LAST green node: the artifact ships its trial evidence to Telegram — a screen recording of an agent using it, the rendered deck, the decision memo with its criteria checked — and the green wave physically cannot reach the root without one human 'yes.' The machine proves self-consistency; the human supplies ground truth. **Why better:** No machine oracle fully captures 'is this what I MEANT,' and the Tower already trusts a human gate for art promotion. One well-framed human approval at the artifact gives the factory a true external oracle exactly where it matters, without reintroducing humans mid-run.
- **No internal oracle at all — ship fast and let the human's reaction be the test** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Stop manufacturing a ground-truth oracle internally. Bias the entire factory toward shipping a runnable artifact as fast as possible plus a one-tap 'this isn't what I meant' button, and treat the human's reaction as the only real oracle. The factory optimizes time-to-first-rejectable-artifact, not time-to-green. **Why better:** The only true oracle for 'did it do what the human MEANT' is the human; every synthetic gate is an expensive proxy that still can't read intent. Inverting toward fast rejectable output gets the real signal sooner and cheaper than building a fortress of tests that only prove self-consistency.
- **'Green' is a lie — replace the wave with a RED-team climb** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Flip the climbing signal entirely. Instead of a green wave proving done, a red-team wave of adversarial agents climbs the tree trying to BREAK each node — produce a counterexample, a missed intent, a vacuous test. A node is 'done' only when the breakers run out of attacks, not when its builder's tests pass. **Why better:** Absence-of-passing-test is weak; absence-of-surviving-attack is strong. This reframes 'done' as 'survived hostile scrutiny' (Popperian falsification) rather than 'confirmed itself' (the confirmation bias baked into green-equals-done), inverting the factory's core success mechanic rather than merely strengthening the oracle bolted onto it.
- **Strip the builder of the green button entirely** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — A leaf the Codex family builds is graded only by a Claude judge re-deriving expected behavior from the original intent string (and vice-versa). The builder's own tests are treated as suspect evidence, not proof; same-family green is recorded but never closes a node — only the opposite family's intent-derived confirmation flips it to done. **Why better:** Directly attacks the stated flaw — tests written by the same family that builds — by making the cross-model split load-bearing for the SUCCESS signal, not just for review. Self-consistency is explicitly demoted from oracle to hint, removing the model's ability to self-certify.

### Graceful degradation & shippable partial artifacts

_Current assumption: The model is all-or-nothing: the green wave reaches the root and a 'finished artifact' falls out. Unstated: real runs will have some leaves that never go green (provider outage, an impossible contract, budget exhaustion mid-run). There is no defined behavior for delivering a PARTIAL artifact — which subtrees are complete-and-shippable vs stubbed, how the system marks a hole (a typed stub, a feature flag, a TODO the user explicitly accepts), and whether the user gets 80% working + a punch-list versus nothing. ArtLab models this (blockers let a run pause without dying); the factory hypothesis assumes binary completion._

**Boldest reframe:** The Artifact Is Always Shippable — There Is No Build, Only a Living Organism: from the instant intent is captured the root node IS deployable (every leaf ships as a typed stub the moment its contract freezes), and the green wave merely upgrades stubs in place while the user is already using it. This is the boldest because it doesn't add graceful-degradation as a feature — it inverts the entire premise so that 'partial' is the ground state and 'complete' is just an asymptote, making an all-or-nothing failure structurally impossible because there was never an all-or-nothing wave to break.

- **Shippable subtree watermark (green-shippable rollup)** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Every node carries a rollup status: a subtree is GREEN-SHIPPABLE only if every leaf under it is green AND its stitch contract is satisfied. The cockpit shades each subtree by this rollup so at any moment you can see the largest complete-and-coherent chunk you could ship right now. **Why better:** Turns 'all-or-nothing at the root' into 'maximal green frontier somewhere in the middle.' A run that stalls at 80% still has a clearly-marked, internally-coherent deliverable instead of an undifferentiated half-built mess.
- **Typed stub as a legal leaf outcome** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — A leaf that can't go green (outage, impossible contract, budget exhausted) resolves to a TYPED STUB satisfying the frozen signature — a sentinel value, a NotImplemented marked with the contract id, or a 'coming soon' panel for a UI floor. The stitch wave treats a typed stub as 'green-but-hollow' so the artifact still compiles and runs. **Why better:** Because contracts freeze top-down BEFORE the build, a stub can always honor the signature — so one dead leaf no longer poisons its whole subtree. You get a running 80% artifact with explicit holes instead of a non-compiling 95%.
- **Auto-generated punch-list as a shipped artifact** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — When a run terminates without full green, the system emits PUNCH-LIST.md alongside the artifact: every stubbed/red leaf, its contract, WHY it failed (outage vs impossible vs budget), and the exact one-shot prompt to finish it later. The punch-list is a first-class factory output, not an error log. **Why better:** The current model gives the user nothing actionable on partial failure. A punch-list converts 'the run didn't finish' into 'here is your 80% plus a precise to-do list you accepted' — and each item is already a Codex-ready leaf for a resume run.
- **User-accepted TODO gate before swarm spend** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Extend the scope-preview gate: the cheap pre-swarm preview flags any leaf the planner already suspects is under-specified, impossible, or provider-risky and asks the user to pre-accept 'ship this as a stub if it fails.' Accepted holes become explicit budgeted TODOs; unaccepted ones block the run. **Why better:** Moves the partial-vs-nothing decision to BEFORE the money is spent, where it's cheap and reversible. The user consents to specific holes up front instead of discovering surprise gaps after a full swarm burn.
- **Degradation budget as a first-class dial** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Add a knob next to the altitude dial: 'minimum acceptable completeness' (e.g. ship at >=70% of leaves green, else abort and refund the rest of the budget). The orchestrator monitors the green frontier live and either delivers the partial at threshold or halts spending before sinking budget into an unreachable root. **Why better:** Reframes graceful degradation as an intentional product choice. It guarantees you never spend the full budget chasing a root you'll never reach, and makes '80% working + punch-list' a target the user explicitly opted into.
- **Feature-flag every hole instead of stubbing silently** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Each unfinished leaf in a buildable app gets wired behind an auto-generated feature flag defaulting OFF, keyed to the contract id. The shipped artifact runs cleanly with holes hidden; flipping a flag later (after a resume run fills the leaf) lights it up with no re-stitch. **Why better:** A typed stub still surfaces a broken-looking UI; a flag makes the partial look intentional and demo-able. It also gives a clean seam for the resume run to slot the finished leaf in without disturbing the green parts.
- **Blocker-to-leaf parity with ArtLab** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Adopt ArtLab's orthogonal-blocker vocabulary on plan-tree leaves: every leaf state is (status, blocker?) where blocker is one of needs-human / budget-blocked / provider-blocked / repair-required / impossible-contract. A blocked leaf PAUSES rather than failing the tree, exactly as an ArtLab run pauses without dying. **Why better:** ArtLab already proved a run can pause-without-dying via typed blockers; the factory lacks this. Reusing the proven vocabulary gives every leaf a precise machine-readable reason it's not green — which powers the punch-list, the watermark, and resume routing.
- **Resume-from-frontier instead of rerun-from-root** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Persist the green frontier and every stub/blocker so a later run re-enters at the holes only — re-reading the still-frozen contracts, rebuilding just the red/stubbed leaves, re-stitching upward from each repaired node. The partial artifact is explicitly a checkpoint, not a throwaway. **Why better:** Makes partial delivery non-wasteful: the 80% is a saved checkpoint. Because contracts froze top-down, the holes stay one-shot-able later, so finishing is cheap and never re-burns the already-green budget.
- **The Artifact Is Always Shippable — There Is No Build, Only a Living Organism** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Kill the notion of a 'run that finishes.' From the instant intent is captured, the root node IS a deployable artifact — every leaf ships as a typed stub the moment the contract freezes (a button rendering 'coming soon', an API returning 501-with-shape, a report section saying 'pending: revenue model'). The green wave doesn't produce the artifact; it upgrades stubs in place, live, while the user is already using it. Cancel any second and you keep exactly what's real. **Why better:** The current assumption bolts 'partial' on as an end-state failure mode. This inverts it: partial is the ground state and complete is the asymptote. There is never a moment where the user has nothing — graceful degradation becomes structurally impossible to violate because there was never an all-or-nothing wave to break.
- **Punch-List as a First-Class Character (a CRO for Holes)** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Every hole the swarm couldn't fill — outage, impossible contract, budget death — is handed to a dedicated agent-character who lives inside the delivered artifact and narrates the gaps: 'Floor 6 networking is live; the contact-enrichment pipe is stubbed because the provider was down — say the word and I'll retry, or here's the one-line manual workaround.' The holes have a voice, personality, and memory, like ArtLab's blockers inhabiting the metaphor. **Why better:** The current model has no defined behavior for telling the user WHAT is missing or WHY. A typed stub is silent. A character converts a cold defect report into the same building-metaphor experience as everything else, making '80% + a list' feel like a feature, not an apology.
- **Severable Contracts — the Plan-Tree Pre-Computes Its Own Amputation Lines** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — When contracts freeze top-down, each subtree also declares its 'severability seam': the exact feature-flag, fallback value, and degraded UX that makes it safely removable without taking neighbors down. The tree knows, before any build, every clean cut-line — so when a leaf dies, the system amputates along a pre-declared seam instead of leaving a jagged crash. The artifact ships missing a limb, not bleeding. **Why better:** Today a dead leaf can poison its whole subtree because nobody decided in advance where it's safe to cut. Pre-computing severability at freeze time means degradation is designed, not discovered — every hole is a clean, flagged, neighbor-isolated absence with a known fallback.
- **The Regret Auction — Budget Death Spends Its Last Dollars on What Hurts Most to Miss** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — When budget or time runs out mid-run, the system doesn't stop at a random frontier. It runs a final micro-auction: each unbuilt leaf bids its 'user-regret cost' (how much the artifact's value collapses if this stays a stub), and the last tokens go to the highest-regret leaves first. You exhaust the budget on the load-bearing wall, never the throw pillow. **Why better:** The current model has no graceful triage — it just fails to reach root. A regret-weighted last-spend turns budget exhaustion from a cliff into a controlled descent that maximizes the value of whatever DID get built, guaranteeing the 80% you keep is the RIGHT 80%.
- **Shippable at Every Altitude — Degrade Down the Tiers, Not Just the Tree** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — If a T3 whole-app run can't complete, it doesn't return a broken T3 — it gracefully collapses to the best honest T2 (a feature), or T1 (a component), or T0, and ships THAT as a complete, coherent artifact with a clear 'this is the floor we reached' marker. The altitude dial becomes a fallback ladder: aim for the skyscraper, deliver a finished townhouse rather than skyscraper rubble. **Why better:** The hypothesis assumes outputs are 'finished T-whatever' or nothing. Coupling degradation to the altitude tiers means a failed ambitious run still yields something whole at a lower tier — the user always receives a complete artifact at SOME altitude, never a half-built one at the target.
- **Time-Travel Holes — Every Stub Carries Its Own Resume Ticket** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Each unfilled leaf ships embedded with a cryptographically-sealed 'resume capsule': the frozen contract, the failing test, the golden template, and the exact graph slice it needed. The user (or a future run, a different day, after the provider recovers) double-clicks the hole and the swarm fills JUST that leaf into the already-shipped artifact — no re-run, no re-plan. The artifact heals itself incrementally over weeks. **Why better:** Currently a partial artifact is a dead end — to fill a hole you re-run the whole thing. Per-hole resume capsules make partiality temporary and surgical: the punch-list becomes a list of one-click buttons that each complete themselves on demand, turning '80% forever' into '80% now, 100% whenever.'
- **The Honesty Contract — the Artifact Cannot Lie About What's Real** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Bake a non-bypassable invariant into the stitch: any stubbed path must be visually and behaviorally truthful at runtime (a stub button dimmed and labeled, a stub API returning a typed 'not-implemented' the UI knows how to render, a stub report section watermarked). The graphify as-built verification checks not just 'does reality match the contract' but 'does the artifact honestly disclose every place reality fell short.' **Why better:** The biggest danger of a partial isn't the hole — it's a hole that LOOKS finished and silently breaks in front of the user. Making honesty a verified invariant means a shipped partial can never masquerade as complete, so the user always knows exactly the 80% they can trust.
- **Two Artifacts Out of Every Run: the Build and Its Autopsy** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Every run emits a twin deliverable — the artifact AND a 'glass-box autopsy': an interactive replay of the plan-tree showing every leaf's final state, why each hole exists, the model/cost/failover trail, and a one-click 'fund the rest' that quotes the exact dollars and minutes to finish the remaining stubs. The autopsy is a navigable floor of the building, not a log file. **Why better:** Right now there's no defined behavior for explaining a partial result. Shipping the autopsy alongside turns every degraded run into a transparent, actionable transaction: you see precisely what you got, what you didn't, and what completing it would cost — silent failure becomes an informed choice.
- **Contracts ship with a born-in degraded form (the 'floor contract')** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — When the top-down contract for any node freezes, it freezes as a PAIR: the full signature AND a minimum-viable-satisfaction variant (the floor). A leaf that can't reach the full contract can still satisfy the floor (e.g. returns a typed empty/placeholder that still type-checks and renders). The green wave can climb on floor-green as well as full-green, tagging each. **Why better:** The current assumption treats a contract as a single all-or-nothing obligation, so one impossible leaf poisons its subtree. A dual full/floor contract means the green wave never chooses between perfect and nothing — it always has a legal lower rung, so partial delivery is structural, not a rescue hack.
- **Holes are typed values, not errors — a first-class Stub<T> in the graph** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Absence becomes a real typed node: a Stub<T> carries the contract it failed to meet, a render-safe placeholder of the right shape, the reason (outage / impossible / budget), and a re-entry handle. Stitch treats a Stub exactly like a satisfied child — it just propagates a 'degraded' tint up the tree. **Why better:** Today a missing leaf has no representation, so it can only break the parent's type and abort. Making the hole itself a typed citizen lets the artifact compile, ship, and self-document where it's hollow — delivering 80% working plus a machine-readable punch-list instead of a stack trace.
- **Ship the frontier, not the root** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Redefine 'the artifact' as the maximal set of complete-and-coherent subtrees (the green frontier), not the root node. Every run is therefore always shippable — at any instant the system can emit the largest internally-consistent slice that's done, with the unfinished remainder presented as named separable modules. **Why better:** The current model only yields a product when the wave reaches the very top, so a 95%-done run delivers zero. Defining delivery at the frontier makes value monotonic — every leaf that goes green strictly increases what the user can take home, and a dead leaf costs only its own subtree.
- **Contracts that auto-renegotiate downward when reality resists** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Give each contract a 'descope ladder' written at freeze time: ordered fallbacks (full → simpler signature → static → omitted-behind-flag). When a leaf fails N times or a blocker fires, the system walks down the ladder automatically and re-freezes the children against the lowered contract instead of stalling. **Why better:** The current assumption fixes the contract and demands reality conform, so an impossible-as-specified leaf hangs forever. A self-lowering contract converts 'impossible' into 'shipped at a lower tier with a logged downgrade' — the run completes at a worse-but-real altitude rather than dying at the intended one.
- **graphify verifies degradation honesty: no silent partials** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Extend the as-built graph check so it verifies not just 'reality matches contract' but 'every gap between reality and the FULL contract is explicitly declared as a Stub/floor/descope.' Any undeclared shortfall — a leaf that quietly returned less than promised — is a hard failure even if it compiles. **Why better:** A SILENTLY degraded run is more dangerous than a loudly broken one. The current hypothesis has no guard against a worker quietly under-delivering; making honesty (declared holes) the verification target ensures what's green is truly green and what's hollow is flagged.
- **Two finished artifacts per run: the degraded-now and the aspirational-full** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Every run continuously maintains two coherent outputs side by side — the best shippable artifact buildable from currently-green-or-floored nodes (deliverable this second), and the full-contract artifact still being chased. The cockpit lets the user 'take the degraded one now' at any moment and keep the swarm chasing the full one in the background. **Why better:** The current model has a single output that only exists at the end, so there's no 'good enough, ship it now' mid-run. Maintaining a live degraded artifact in parallel decouples 'I have something usable' from 'the build is perfect' — the user is never held hostage to the slowest or most impossible leaf.
- **Keep-going build, not stop-the-line (--keep-going with a per-leaf go/no-go ledger)** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Steal Bazel/Make's --keep-going. When a leaf fails, the orchestrator does NOT halt the wave — it marks that subtree red, skips only the leaves that transitively depend on its contract, and keeps building every independent subtree to green. The run ends with a Bazel-style summary: N built, M failed, K skipped-because-upstream-failed. **Why better:** The current assumption is stop-the-line: one un-green leaf and the whole artifact is withheld. Real DAGs have parallel branches that don't depend on the failed one — --keep-going delivers every shippable subtree instead of throwing away 80% of completed independent work because 20% choked.
- **Compensation/saga semantics: every leaf ships with an undo, retreat to a clean boundary** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Borrow Temporal/Saga compensation. Each leaf registers a compensating action when it goes green. If a sibling subtree dies and would leave the artifact half-wired (a route to a page never built, a migration with no consumer), the orchestrator runs compensations up to the nearest consistent cut — delivering a smaller-but-coherent artifact rather than a larger broken one. **Why better:** Binary completion ignores that a partial build can be WORSE than coherent-and-smaller (dangling refs, orphan schema). Sagas give a principled 'retreat to the last consistent line' so the partial artifact is always internally valid, never a Frankenstein.
- **Manufacturing rework lane: a failed leaf is diverted off the conveyor, not a line-stop** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Translate an assembly line's andon + rework loop. A failed leaf isn't a halt; it's a part diverted to a rework station (retry with a fatter model, a different stack template, or a human). The main conveyor keeps moving and the artifact ships with the reworked part either hot-swapped in late or flagged as scrap on the final QA sheet. **Why better:** The factory hypothesis treats every failure as a full-line stop. A rework queue lets one defective node be repaired asynchronously without freezing the other 200 nodes — andon stops the whole line only for an uncontainable defect, everything else gets a lane.
- **VFX temp-comp / proxy renders: grey-box placeholders make the artifact walkable from minute one** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Steal the film pipeline's temp-comp culture: a shot is never blank, it's a grey-box proxy until the final render lands. Every leaf has a deterministic cheap placeholder (lorem UI, stub copy, a 1-line mock function, a wireframe component) generated at CONTRACT-freeze time. The artifact is whole-and-walkable from minute one; green leaves progressively replace their proxies. **Why better:** All-or-nothing means the user sees NOTHING until the root goes green, then maybe a hole. Temp comps invert it: the user always has a complete clickable artifact whose unfinished parts are obviously grey — vastly better for early review, demo, and deciding which holes are worth filling.
- **Shippability as a reconciler-computed graph attribute (a 'completeness frontier')** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Extend ArtLab's (phase, blocker?) reconciler upward: instead of asking 'did the root go green?', the reconciler continuously computes a SHIPPABILITY FRONTIER over the plan-tree — the maximal set of subtrees that are green-and-coherent right now. At any instant the cockpit can emit 'the largest shippable artifact available' plus the punch-list of everything below the frontier. **Why better:** ArtLab already proved a run's state is (phase, blocker?) read through one reconciler — but the factory reverts to binary at the root. Lifting the reconciler to compute a frontier means there is ALWAYS a defined deliverable partial, and 'done' becomes 'frontier == root' rather than a separate concept.
- **Budget as Nx-style 'affected' triage: last tokens to the highest-value reachable subtree** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Borrow Nx/Turborepo 'affected' + priority scheduling. When budget exhaustion is imminent mid-run, the orchestrator re-plans: rank ungreen leaves by user-declared value × cheapness-to-green, spend the last tokens to maximize shipped value, and auto-stub the long tail with a punch-list. **Why better:** Today budget death is undefined and effectively random — whatever leaf was mid-flight dies and the run aborts. Value-weighted triage turns a hard budget wall into a graceful 'we shipped the 80% that mattered, here's the priced punch-list for the rest.'
- **Apoptosis: an impossible leaf cleanly self-terminates and emits a signed 'hole certificate'** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Steal programmed cell death from biology. Some contracts are genuinely impossible (a self-contradicting spec, an API that doesn't exist). Rather than retry-storm until budget dies, the leaf runs a quick falsifiability probe; if it concludes 'no green state exists' it apoptoses — emits a HOLE CERTIFICATE (why it's impossible, what the user must change or accept) and the parent treats it as a deliberately-accepted typed stub the user co-signs. **Why better:** The hypothesis has no notion of an impossible contract — it would retry or hang forever, burning budget and delivering nothing. Apoptosis makes impossibility a fast, cheap, graceful outcome with an auditable certificate, converting an infinite failure mode into an explicit user-acknowledged hole.
- **Quorum / degraded-mode delivery: each node declares its own 'done-enough' green-percentage** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Let each plan node carry a degradation policy: 'this subtree ships at >=80% green leaves', 'this one is all-or-nothing (auth, payments)', 'this one is best-effort'. The stitch wave climbs as soon as a node meets its OWN quorum, not when 100% of children are green — so non-critical breadth degrades gracefully while critical spines stay strict. **Why better:** Binary completion applies the same strictness to a decorative empty-state and to the login flow. Per-node quorum lets the factory be ruthless where correctness is sacred and forgiving where breadth is nice-to-have — the green wave reaches a meaningful root far more often, with the right things guaranteed.
- **Partial delivery is a lie detector for a broken contract — delete it, fail loud** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Inverting the assumption: a leaf that never goes green is not a 'hole to ship around' — it is PROOF the top-down contract was wrong (impossible signature, under-specified leaf, mis-scoped tier). Graceful degradation lets a bad contract masquerade as a 90%-done artifact, hiding the one signal that should halt and re-architect. Kill partial-delivery; a red leaf hard-aborts the subtree and forces a contract re-freeze at the lowest ancestor that can absorb the change. **Why better:** The whole value of freezing contracts top-down is that a leaf failure is diagnostic. Shipping 80% + a punch-list converts a loud architectural signal into a quiet pile of TODOs the user rubber-stamps, and you lose the one moment where the plan-tree should have learned it was wrong.
- **There is no 'partial artifact' — only a smaller artifact that IS whole** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Don't deliver a punch-listed cripple of the big thing; re-plan the failed subtree OUT and deliver the largest complete subtree as a genuinely finished smaller artifact. If the auth floor can't go green, the factory hands you the four floors that DO work as a real shippable mini-app and tells you auth was descoped. The altitude dial drops a tier instead of the artifact developing holes. **Why better:** A 'partial' artifact with stubs is neither shippable nor honest — every stub is a trap. A smaller-but-whole artifact preserves the core promise (intent in, FINISHED artifact out) and reuses the tier machinery you already have instead of inventing a hole-marking ontology.
- **Merge degradation into the scope-gate, before the swarm spends — not after** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — The question 'what do we do when leaves don't go green at the end' is the scope-preview gate's job done too late. Move all degradation reasoning UPSTREAM: at the cheap pre-swarm gate the system predicts fragile/impossible leaves (provider risk, unsatisfiable contract, budget headroom) and the user pre-commits scope. There is no post-hoc partial mode because the run only ever starts on a subtree it can finish. **Why better:** Post-hoc partial handling burns the budget THEN discovers the hole — the worst ordering. Folding it into the existing scope gate means the user accepts the smaller scope before spending, which is cheaper, more honest, and removes an entire all-or-nothing failure surface instead of patching it.
- **A factory that ships holes is a code generator with extra steps — keep the binary bar as the moat** `small/rash` _(curated)_ — The defining claim is 'finished artifact falls out.' The moment you institutionalize typed stubs, feature flags, and accepted-TODOs you've rebuilt Copilot: a thing that emits mostly-working scaffolding a human must finish. Delete partial-delivery to PROTECT the category — the binary completion bar is the entire differentiator, not an oversight. **Why better:** Every assistant already ships 80% + a punch-list; that's the commodity the factory exists to beat. Treating all-or-nothing as a bug to fix optimizes the product back into the crowded middle. The constraint IS the moat.
- **Invert who absorbs the hole: a red leaf is a bug report against the PLANNER, not a flag for the user** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — When a leaf won't go green, the opposite of 'mark a hole and move on' is 'route the failure UP as a defect against the node that authored that contract.' The user never sees a stub; the planning agent that froze an unsatisfiable signature does, and re-plans. Degradation becomes an internal self-healing loop of the plan-tree, not an external punch-list. **Why better:** Punch-lists externalize the system's own planning errors onto the user — the worst-placed party to fix a leaf the swarm couldn't. Bouncing the failure to the contract author keeps the repair inside the model's competence and turns failures into planner training signal.
- **Outage and budget-exhaustion are PAUSE, not PARTIAL — steal ArtLab's blocker verbatim** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — The aspect conflates two failures: 'this leaf is impossible' (contract bug) and 'this leaf is temporarily blocked' (provider down, budget gone). For the second, the correct inversion of 'ship a partial' is 'don't ship — freeze and resume,' exactly as ArtLab's blockers pause a run without killing it. No partial-artifact concept is needed; there's a paused run with a resumable frontier. **Why better:** Most real-run holes are transient (outage, quota), not structural. Treating them as permanent holes-to-ship-around throws away work that would have completed on resume an hour later. ArtLab already proves pause-and-resume beats partial-delivery for this failure class.
- **Holes are contagious — a stub at depth 5 silently rots every green ancestor above it** `small/rash` _(curated)_ — The hidden lie in 'shippable partial' is that the green wave above a stub is FAKE green: the parent only stitched because the stub satisfied the contract's TYPE, not its behavior. So an 80%-complete artifact isn't 80% trustworthy — its completed regions are unverified wherever they transitively depend on a hole. Better to refuse the climb past a stub than to manufacture false confidence up the whole spine. **Why better:** Graphify's as-built verification can't distinguish a real green leaf from a type-satisfying stub once the wave passes it. Partial delivery therefore corrupts the system's central integrity claim. Blocking the wave at the stub keeps 'green' meaning 'actually works,' worth more than a higher completion percentage.
- **Replace the punch-list with a single honest verdict: SHIPPABLE or NOT — no middle drawer** `small/rash` _(curated)_ — Delete the spectrum (complete / stubbed / flagged / accepted-TODO) and collapse it to one bit per delivered subtree. The factory's output isn't 'here's 80% and a to-do list'; it's 'here is the set of subtrees I will stake my name on as done' and nothing else crosses the line. The accepted-TODO category — where the user 'explicitly accepts' a hole — is the most dangerous and should not exist. **Why better:** An 'accepted TODO' is how every hole gets laundered into a shipped product: the user clicks accept under time pressure and inherits a landmine. A binary shippable/not verdict removes the laundering path and forces the system to either finish a thing or explicitly hand it back, never to hand over ambiguity dressed as progress.

### Run forensics & the post-mortem trail (distinct from the live cockpit)

_Current assumption: The cockpit is framed as a LIVE watch view (tree, badges, status, gates) — observation is implicitly real-time-only. Unstated: when a run finishes wrong, or partially, you need AFTER-THE-FACT forensics — a queryable event log per leaf (every prompt, model, tool call, verifier verdict, retry, failover, the diff each worker produced), so you can answer 'why is this leaf broken', 'where did the budget go', 'which worker introduced the regression'. ArtLab already writes append-only events.jsonl + receipts per run for exactly this. The cockpit shows the present; nothing in the seed owns the durable, replayable audit trail of the past._

**Boldest reframe:** Counterfactual / knockout replay — re-execute a single leaf from its frozen contract + captured inputs with ONE variable changed (other model, higher budget, reverted parent output, patched contract) and diff the alternate timeline against what shipped. This is the boldest reframe because it converts the post-mortem from narration into EXPERIMENT: instead of forming a hypothesis about why a leaf went wrong, the trail proves the cause by re-running it green — and as a side effect makes the two-model router self-improving (every autopsy yields evidence about which model should own which node-type).

- **Per-leaf append-only event ledger (events.jsonl, reused verbatim)** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Every leaf in the plan-tree writes an append-only events.jsonl in ArtLab's existing {runId, at, kind, payload} shape, capturing each prompt, model badge, tool call, verifier verdict, retry, and failover as ordered events. The cockpit reads the tail live; the post-mortem reads the whole file. **Why better:** The seed assumes only live state exists; this gives a durable, replayable trail per leaf on an already-proven primitive, so 'what happened on this leaf' is answerable after the run ends, not just while it streams.
- **Diff receipt per worker attempt** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Extend ArtLab's CreativeBudgetReceipt into a build receipt: every worker attempt records the exact diff it produced (or hash + path), the leaf contract it targeted, the model, cents, and pass/fail verdict. A leaf's history becomes an ordered list of attempt receipts. **Why better:** Lets you answer 'which worker/attempt introduced this regression' by reading diffs attributed to attempts, instead of git-blaming a squashed stitch commit where authorship is lost.
- **Verifier-verdict provenance chain** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Each leaf records WHY it was marked green: which verifier ran (tower-ship-gate, tsc, a failing test going green, a Codex cross-review), the verdict, and the exact pasted output. A red-after-stitch leaf shows the precise gate that should have caught it. **Why better:** When a run finishes wrong you can see whether a leaf was actually verified or rubber-stamped — the green wave is trusted today without preserving the evidence behind each green.
- **Frozen-contract vs as-built drift report** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — At post-mortem, diff the contract frozen top-down for each leaf (typed signature, schema, failing tests) against what graphify sees as-built, and list every leaf where reality diverged from its contract. **Why better:** The seed says graphify already does as-built verification; persisting that comparison per leaf turns it into a forensic artifact that pinpoints contract violations, where the cockpit only shows live status, not the durable record of which leaves drifted.
- **Time-travel scrubber / DVR — drag a slider, watch the tree rebuild** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Because events are append-only and timestamped, reconstruct the full plan-tree state at any past instant. A scrubber lets you scrub to 14:32 and SEE which leaves were green, which worker was mid-prompt, the budget, and where failover fired — a deterministic replay of the run's history rendered in the SAME cockpit UI, with no separate forensics screen. `forge replay <runId>` is the entry point. **Why better:** The cockpit is assumed live-only and progress.json overwrites the past; an append-only log IS a timeline, so the same UI fed historical events becomes a DVR, collapsing the false split between live-watch and after-the-fact forensics into one rewindable view.
- **Regression bisect over the deterministic stitch order** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Because the stitch is a deterministic bottom-up wave with a known-good root and known-bad tip, record the merge sequence and let `forge bisect <failing-test>` binary-search the build, replaying leaf states at the midpoint and running the failing verifier until it names the first leaf-merge where the symptom appears — output 'leaf 7.3, Codex attempt #2 after Claude failover, diff line 42.' **Why better:** Turns 'which leaf broke the build' from manual archaeology into a mechanical O(log n) search, leveraging the total order the factory already knows — the human stops being the search algorithm over a flat log designed for a single run rather than a tree.
- **Autonomous forensics agent — git-bisect for blame, run by an LLM** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — When a stitched run lands broken, an autonomous forensics agent walks the event DAG bottom-up, re-running the failing verifier against each leaf's diff in dependency order to isolate the exact worker + exact edit that introduced the regression, then writes a one-paragraph indictment with the offending diff hunk highlighted. **Why better:** Pairs the mechanical bisect with an agent that authors the verdict, so 'which worker introduced the regression' is answered — culprit leaf AND guilty line — before a human even opens the cockpit.
- **Self-writing root-cause card the moment a run goes red** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — On any failure or quality-gate miss, an LLM forensic analyst is auto-spawned that reads the leaf's full event slice (prompts, retries, failover, verdicts, diff) and emits a structured root-cause card: symptom, suspected cause, smoking-gun event, cheapest fix, confidence. No human opens a raw log unless they want to contest the card. **Why better:** The cheapest reader of a leaf's audit trail is an LLM that already understands the contract; the durable artifact of a failed run should be a generated root-cause card with the raw log as citation, not a log a human must spelunk.
- **Auto-emitted post-mortem digest on non-clean finish** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — When a run ends partial or wrong, auto-generate a one-page digest from the ledgers: failed leaves, the failing verifier output, the suspect diffs, spend overruns, and every failover event — the forensic equivalent of ArtLab's run receipts, shareable and diffable across runs. **Why better:** A failed run otherwise leaves you to spelunk raw state; a digest surfaces the 'why is this broken' answer immediately and travels without re-opening the cockpit.
- **Budget/cost autopsy flame-graph over the plan-tree** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Project the event log into a cost-and-token flame-graph where node width = dollars/tokens and color = waste (retries, failovers, rejected verifier loops, abandoned counterfactuals). One glance shows the leaf that ate 40% of the budget on three failed retries; click a hot node to see its attempts. **Why better:** 'Where did the budget go' is an explicit unanswered question in the seed; cost is a property of the tree, so rendering spend as a flame-graph answers it pre-attentively instead of summing scattered receipt payloads, and fits the Bloomberg-Terminal aesthetic.
- **Structured causal trace spans, not log lines (OpenTelemetry model)** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Model each leaf's life as a span tree (plan → contract-freeze → build attempt → tool-call → verifier → failover) with cost, tokens, model, and latency as span attributes, propagating a trace-id down the plan-tree. 'Where did the budget go' becomes a flame graph; 'which worker was slow/expensive' becomes the widest bar — and industry-standard trace UIs/exporters work on it for free. **Why better:** events.jsonl is flat with no causal nesting, so cost/latency attribution needs manual joins; a span model gives hierarchical, queryable attribution natively in a shape existing tooling already understands.
- **The Dailies Room — auto-curated failure reel of every take** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Borrowing VFX dailies, persist EVERY attempt's diff per leaf as a numbered take (take 1 Claude, take 2 Codex-failover, take 3 retry) with the verifier's verdict on each, and auto-assemble a filmstrip post-mortem showing the rejected takes beside the one that shipped. A leaf is explained by contrast — the path not taken next to the path taken. **Why better:** The winning output erases the context of the losers today; making rejected takes first-class durable artifacts with verdicts attached explains a leaf by what was rejected and why, not just by asserting its final state.
- **Andon-cord freeze-frame snapshot at the instant of failure** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Like pulling a Toyota line's andon cord, when a verifier fails a leaf hard or budget burns past a threshold, automatically snapshot the full forensic envelope at that instant — worktree diff, in-flight prompt, parent hashes, partial tool transcript, budget ledger frame — as one immutable capture attached to the node, BEFORE the orchestrator retries or fails over and overwrites context. **Why better:** Retries and failover keep writing events, so by investigation time the precise moment-of-failure state is buried; the andon capture preserves the crime scene at the stop — the single highest-signal frame — instead of forcing reconstruction from the stream.
- **Natural-language interrogation — 'ask the dead run a question'** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — A chat panel over the run's full event+receipt+diff corpus as a queryable RAG index: 'why is the war-room leaf broken?', 'which worker touched auth?', 'show me every failover and what triggered it', 'rank leaves by retry count' — answers cite the exact event lines and diff hunks. **Why better:** The cockpit shows the present and the seed admits nothing owns the past; a conversational query layer makes 50 leaves of JSONL interrogable in English with citations, replacing grep-archaeology with an oracle any non-expert or future agent can question.
- **Content-addressed forensic cache keys — diff a failure against its nearest prior success** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Borrowing Bazel/Nx remote-cache hashing, key every leaf by a hash of (contract signature + prompt + model + tool versions + parent outputs). The forensic trail then answers 'why is this leaf broken' as a cache-miss explanation: 'this leaf differs from the last green build of the same key ONLY in model=Codex and parent-output-hash, so the regression is one of those two.' **Why better:** Receipts hash content but the log treats every run as novel; a hash-keyed history lets you auto-diff a failure against the nearest prior success and attribute the delta, converting 'read the whole story' into 'show me only what changed since this last worked' — across runs.
- **Provenance DAG fused into graphify (manufacturing lot-traceability)** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Make graphify dual-purpose: alongside the code/knowledge graph, every node carries provenance edges — which contract froze it, which parent outputs it consumed, which worker/model/prompt produced it. A single content-addressed/Merkle-chained graph query — 'all leaves downstream of contract C v2' — does instant recall AND forward impact analysis when one upstream contract turns out to be the root cause, and detects after the fact if any worker quietly diverged from its frozen contract. **Why better:** The log records EVENTS (what happened), not LINEAGE (what derived from what); a content-addressed provenance DAG makes 'which worker introduced this' a hash lookup, makes contract-divergence cryptographically detectable, and answers recall + blast-radius questions a flat per-run log fundamentally can't.
- **Post-mortem feeds back into the planner as a typed 'lesson'** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — On every run that finished wrong or over-budget, a judge-pass auto-drafts a structured post-mortem (root cause, blast radius, budget leak, which contract was under-specified) AND emits a typed lesson the NEXT plan-tree consults — e.g. 'leaves of type X under stack Y need a tighter golden template' becomes a planning prior. **Why better:** The seed treats forensics as read-only history; closing the loop so post-mortems mutate future plans turns the audit trail into the factory's memory — every failure makes the next run cheaper and likelier to pass instead of being a corpse nobody reads twice.
- **Regression-memory 'scar tissue' — failed runs become the next run's test corpus** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Every post-mortem that pins a root cause auto-distills a tiny failing fixture (the exact prompt + contract + the wrong output) into a scar-tissue ledger (like ArtLab's memory/*.jsonl taste signals). Future runs replay the scar corpus as a pre-flight regression gate, so the factory literally cannot re-make a mistake it has already diagnosed. **Why better:** The most valuable output of forensics is a TEST, not a story; feeding diagnosed failures back as regression fixtures makes the factory's defect rate monotonically fall instead of resetting every run, reframing the trail from backward-looking explanation to forward-looking prevention.
- **Cross-run epidemiology — diff THIS failure against every prior run** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Don't analyze a broken run in isolation; query the whole corpus of past runs' logs to find that this exact failure signature ('Codex leaf fails strict-qa after Claude failover on contracts with >5 fields') has now happened 9 times. The forensic verdict carries a population, not an anecdote: 'this is a systemic worker-routing flaw, not a one-off.' **Why better:** The unit of work (a run, siloed at runs/<runId>/events.jsonl) is not the unit of insight; promoting forensics from per-run to cross-run epidemiology turns scattered anecdotes into a diagnosable pattern library that tells you whether to fix one leaf or fix the router.
- **Counterfactual / knockout replayer — re-execute a leaf with ONE variable changed** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Treat events.jsonl not as a read-only diary but as a re-executable script: every leaf records its exact frozen contract, prompt, model, seed, and tool inputs, so any leaf can be replayed in isolation — and replayed WITH ONE VARIABLE CHANGED (swap Codex↔Claude, bump temperature, edit the contract, revert an upstream parent output). It then diffs the counterfactual artifact against what shipped, reporting e.g. 'the regression survives a model swap but dies when parent-leaf-7's output is reverted, so leaf 7 is the true cause.' **Why better:** A log tells you WHAT happened; a re-executable trail lets you PROVE the cause (re-run the broken leaf, change one input, watch it go green) instead of guessing — turning post-mortem from narration into a biology-style knockout experiment, and making the two-model router self-improving by producing evidence about which model should own which node-type.
- **Temporal-style event-sourced replay debugger with step/rewind/branch** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Borrow Temporal's event-sourcing determinism: make every leaf's worker a deterministic function of its event history so re-feeding the log replays a run EXACTLY, then expose a debugger with step/rewind/branch buttons — fork a leaf ('replay but with model B / contract patched / new seed') and watch the alternate timeline diverge frame-by-frame as diffs materialize into ghosted worktrees and verifiers flip red/green. **Why better:** The seed stops at a queryable past-tense log you can read but not re-run; if the log fully determines execution, the post-mortem and the fix become the SAME action — you reproduce the failure and test a candidate fix from the exact prior state instead of re-launching the whole swarm and hoping.
- **Cryptographic provenance — every artifact carries a signed, hash-chained receipt** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Each shipped file embeds (sidecar or commit trailer) a hash-chained provenance manifest: which leaf produced it, under which contract hash, which model, which verifier verdicts, which budget — a Merkle-style causal ledger. Anyone can later prove 'this exact line was written by Codex under contract v3, passed tower-ship-gate, cost $0.04' — tamper-evident, non-repudiable, like ArtLab's byte-protection but for causality. **Why better:** events.jsonl can drift from reality (the scanner already counts malformedLines); a hash-chained, artifact-embedded receipt makes the trail as-built-verifiable and gives graphify's 'does reality match the contract' question a cryptographic yes/no instead of a best-effort scan.
- **Black-box flight recorder + crash siren that resurrects the run** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Treat each run like an aircraft: a tamper-proof flight-data recorder captures the last N decisions before any crash at full fidelity, and on failure a siren auto-packages a self-contained crash bundle (events, receipts, diffs, env, contract hashes) that can be re-hydrated into a fresh worktree to resume EXACTLY from the last green leaf — no human reconstruction. **Why better:** The seed is passive observation; a flight recorder + resurrectable crash bundle means a wrong/partial run isn't a dead end you investigate — it's a saved game you reload one leaf before the failure and re-launch the swarm, turning post-mortems into instant recovery.
- **Adversarial self-interrogating post-mortem (knockout agent over a replayable log)** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — After a wrong run, spawn a cheap reflective agent that reads the trace and runs targeted knockouts/swaps from the replayable state — re-run the suspect leaf with the OTHER model, with the verifier's own counter-prompt, or with one upstream input reverted — and reports which intervention makes the defect die, localizing the true root cause autonomously. The forensic equivalent of the two-model judge, pointed at the past. **Why better:** Every readability idea leaves the human to form and test hypotheses; a reflective agent driving knockouts over a replayable log makes the trail INTERROGATE ITSELF, so the factory localizes its own root cause without a human scrolling.
- **Kill forensics — make the build self-healing instead of self-documenting** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Delete the after-the-fact audit trail as a first-class concern. A run that finishes wrong is a run that failed verification, so the answer is not a queryable log of why but an autonomous retry/repair loop that re-derives the leaf until it's green. If you never ship a broken leaf you never need to explain one — forensics is a confession that the verifier was too weak; fix the verifier, not the autopsy. **Why better:** The seed treats broken output as inevitable and invests in explaining it; inverting that pours the same effort upstream into making broken output not survive to the post-mortem at all — where it changes outcomes instead of merely narrating them.
- **Forensics is the cockpit paused — there is no separate 'past' subsystem** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Reject the premise that live-watch and post-mortem are distinct aspects. The cockpit IS the forensic view; 'after the fact' is simply the cockpit with the clock stopped and time-travel enabled. Merge the aspect entirely: one event-sourced tree you can scrub backward, with no separate forensics store, schema, or query language. **Why better:** The seed itself frames forensics as 'distinct from the live cockpit' — that split is the mistake; a single rewindable timeline is cheaper, has zero sync risk between two stores, and makes every live affordance (badges, diffs, gate state) automatically a forensic affordance for free.
- **Don't store the trail — regenerate the explanation on demand from the diff** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Stop writing a durable per-leaf event log at all. Keep only the cheap, already-versioned artifacts: the frozen contract, the failing tests, and the git diff each worker produced. When you ask 'why is this leaf broken', spin up a fresh judge agent that reads those three and reconstructs the causal story live. The explanation is a derived view, not a stored asset. **Why better:** An append-only events.jsonl rots, balloons, and still can't answer novel questions you didn't log fields for; a regenerated explanation answers ANY question, is never stale relative to the code, and costs nothing to maintain because git + the contract are already the real source of truth.
- **Provenance lives IN the artifact, not beside it — the codebase is the audit trail** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Invert where the trail lives: instead of a log sitting next to each leaf, every produced file carries an inline provenance header (which contract clause, which model, which template, which verifier verdict signed it off). The codebase itself becomes the audit trail; since graphify already verifies as-built-vs-contract, the 'why' is queryable by reading the very thing you're suspicious of. **Why better:** A sidecar log can drift from or outlive the code it describes; provenance welded into the artifact can never desync, travels with the file through merges and reverts, and turns 'which worker introduced the regression' into a one-line blame query instead of a cross-referenced log dig.
- **Ban forensics to force fail-fast aborts** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Argue the post-mortem trail is actively harmful: it makes operators tolerant of letting bad runs complete because 'we can always investigate later.' Remove it, and the only sane policy becomes abort-on-first-contract-violation. A factory that can't explain its failures after the fact is a factory forced to never produce them. **Why better:** The unstated assumption is that you WANT a rich record of failures; the inversion is that wanting it is the disease, because it subsidizes accepting partial/wrong output — removing the 'we can audit later' safety net changes operator behavior toward stopping the swarm the instant the contract graph diverges.
- **Collapse forensics to one budget ledger and nothing else** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Most of the stated need ('where did the budget go', 'which model', 'how many retries') is accounting, not forensics. Collapse the whole replayable trail to one append-only cost ledger per run — tokens, model, dollars, per node. Throw away the prompt/tool-call/diff capture; if a leaf is broken you re-run it, you don't excavate it. **Why better:** The seed bundles two genuinely different needs — money-tracking (durable, simple, always wanted) and causal-debugging (expensive, rarely consulted, goes stale); keeping only the cheap half queried daily and dropping the expensive half nobody opens twice is a better cost/value trade than one heavyweight subsystem.
- **The dispatch manifest IS the historian — no separate post-mortem owner** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Don't give forensics its own home; fold it into the autonomous orchestrator's existing shared manifest, which already names every node, model, and status. Let it be the canonical queryable record by simply never deleting completed entries — the durable replayable audit trail is the manifest at rest. **Why better:** The seed says nothing owns the durable trail, but the manifest already owns dispatch truth; promoting it to also be the historical record avoids inventing a second data structure that must be kept consistent with the dispatcher, eliminating a whole class of 'log says X but the run did Y' bugs.
- **Ephemeral-with-pin — log nothing unless flagged or a verdict trips** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Flip the default: runs keep zero forensic data, and you opt INTO capture per-run with a --record flag, or capture auto-pins only when a verifier fails. The factory is a stateless machine; the rare run you need to dissect is the one you knew was risky going in or the one that tripped a verdict. Everything else evaporates on green. **Why better:** Append-only-everything assumes every run is worth remembering, but with massively parallel swarms 99% are uneventful greens whose logs are pure storage tax and noise that buries the one run you care about — defaulting to forget with surgical pinning makes the signal trivially findable and the footprint near-zero.

### Run-over-run diffing & idempotent re-runs on an evolving target

_Current assumption: Each invocation is treated as a fresh build from intent. Unstated: the realistic loop is ITERATIVE — the user runs the factory, gets an artifact, then says 'now change this one thing' or 'the contract shifted, rebuild.' There is no model for a SECOND run against an already-built tree: what's reused vs rebuilt, how an unchanged subtree is left byte-stable (not silently regenerated by a nondeterministic worker), how the new plan-tree diffs against the prior one, and how local human edits made between runs are preserved rather than clobbered. The factory is framed as fire-once, but it lives in an edit loop._

**Boldest reframe:** The Factory Never Stops — there is no "second run," only a living reconciliation loop (Kubernetes-controller model)

- **Run ledger: persist prior tree, hashes, contracts, and artifact map as a committed manifest** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Write the whole prior run — plan-tree, every node's content hash, contract, and the file paths it produced — to a versioned `.forge/run.json` checked in beside the code. The next run reads this ledger as its baseline; there is no diff, reuse, lock, or edit-detection without it. It travels with the repo so re-runs work on any machine. **Why better:** Diffing, hashing, locking, and edit-detection all need a remembered 'last state'; today each run starts from intent with no memory of the artifact it already built. This is the small enabling primitive that makes every other run-over-run idea possible.
- **Content-address every node; matching input-hash makes regeneration structurally unreachable** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Make the factory a Nix/Bazel-style pure function over the plan-tree. Each node's output is content-addressed by the hash of its frozen contract (signature + schema slice + failing tests + golden template) + its children's hashes + the worker recipe (prompt + model+version) + resolved dependency-leaf hashes. On re-run, a node whose input-closure hash is unchanged returns its cached artifact byte-for-byte — the nondeterministic worker is literally never invoked for it. Diffing two runs collapses to diffing two Merkle roots, O(changed) not O(tree). **Why better:** The fire-once model hopes a worker regenerates an unchanged subtree identically; this makes identical-input-implies-identical-output a hard invariant enforced by hashing, not a hope. It kills silent nondeterministic regeneration at the root — exactly how Bazel/Turborepo/Nix make giant rebuilds cheap and reproducible.
- **Contract-hash is the leaf's identity; matching contract = generation forbidden** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Stop identifying a leaf by file path or output bytes — identify it by a content-hash of its frozen contract alone (typed signature + schema slice + the failing tests it must satisfy). On a second run, if the contract-hash is unchanged, the worker is structurally FORBIDDEN from regenerating that node; the prior build is copied byte-for-byte. Only a changed contract-hash unlocks a worker. Reuse is a property of contracts holding, not of tree-node identity matching. **Why better:** Tree-to-tree diffing is brittle because the planner is nondeterministic — node identities won't line up run to run. Contracts are the stable, human-meaningful unit, so idempotency falls out of the architecture the factory already has (frozen contracts + tests) instead of bolting on a separate reconciler. Generalizes ArtLab's byte-diff-on-promoted-assets gate upward.
- **Self-stabilizing leaves — a leaf is forbidden to change its output if its contract didn't** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Give each leaf-worker a constitutional rule: 'if your contract and inputs are byte-identical to last time, you may emit nothing but your prior output.' Enforce with a post-generation gate that diffs against the cached artifact and, on spurious drift, rejects the generation and replays the cache. Nondeterminism is caged at the node boundary instead of leaking upward into the stitch. **Why better:** Cheaper and more local than a global content-addressed store — a per-leaf tripwire that turns any worker (even a fundamentally nondeterministic LLM) into an effectively-pure function from the tree's point of view, with zero changes to the orchestrator.
- **Determinism / golden-master gate quarantines a rebuilt leaf that drifts beyond its contract delta** `small/rash` _(curated)_ — On a leaf's first successful build, freeze its output as a GOLDEN master. On any re-run that legitimately re-executes that leaf (because inputs changed), run a determinism gate: diff new output against the golden; if the diff exceeds the contract delta — the worker changed things it had no reason to touch — flag it as drift, quarantine it, and require re-convergence or human review before it enters the stitch. **Why better:** Even with caching, a leaf that DOES legitimately rebuild can have a nondeterministic worker rewrite unrelated lines, smuggling churn into a 'one thing changed' run. Statistical-process-control plus golden-master testing makes the diff you get the diff you asked for, not the diff the model felt like producing.
- **Idempotency assertion: re-running identical intent must touch zero files** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Add a cheap self-check mode where re-running the exact same intent against an existing ledger must produce a byte-identical tree and touch zero files. If any worker would change a byte on a no-op re-run, that's a flagged nondeterminism bug, surfaced in the cockpit rather than silently shipped. **Why better:** Idempotence is asserted nowhere today, so silent drift is invisible until it corrupts a diff. Making 'same intent in → same artifact out' a testable invariant turns idempotence from a hope into a guardrail you'd trust before letting a swarm loose.
- **Plan-tree diff as the unit of work — reconcile the tree, don't rebuild it (React virtual-DOM)** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — When intent changes, generate the NEW plan-tree, diff it node-by-node against the stored prior tree matched by stable durable keys (not position), and emit a patch set: added / removed / contract-changed / moved / unchanged. The swarm acts only on the patch. The scope-preview gate that already guards spend now previews the delta — 'this edit touches 2 of 340 leaves' — so the user approves a diff, not a fresh build. **Why better:** Today the scope gate previews a from-scratch build every time, so changing 'one thing' still costs a full tower. A keyed reconciler turns a small intent change into a small surgical patch and makes the gate a real 'here's what your edit actually touches' moment — the React insight that the cheapest re-render is the one you can prove you don't need.
- **Stable durable node IDs minted at creation — deterministic replay against a manifest (Temporal)** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Give every plan-tree node a content-independent durable ID minted at first creation and carried in the manifest, so re-running with a reordered or reworded plan still re-identifies 'this is the same auth leaf as last time.' Re-runs replay the manifest deterministically: same node ID + same inputs => reuse the recorded result; only genuinely new IDs execute. **Why better:** Without stable identity a second run can't tell 'same leaf, slightly reworded' from 'brand-new leaf,' so it rebuilds everything and loses continuity. Temporal/Inngest survive crashes and re-invocations precisely by replaying a durable event history against stable step IDs — giving the factory true idempotency where a tweak touches only the tweak.
- **Intent-diff, not artifact-diff — diff what you MEANT, compute the provably-minimal rebuild** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Before touching a single file, the factory semantically diffs the new intent against the old at the plan-tree level ('you didn't change the schema, you renamed a UI label'), derives the provably-minimal set of leaves to rebuild, and proves the rest are unaffected. The blast radius is computed from meaning, up front, not from a file-system diff after a full regen does the damage. **Why better:** File-diffing after a full regen is closing the barn door late; this front-loads the decision so 95% of leaves are never even dispatched. The scope gate can show 'this edit touches 2 of 340 leaves' before spending a cent.
- **Contract-firewall dirty-propagation — body-only change stops; only signature changes punch through** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Split each leaf's contract into a public SIGNATURE (the typed interface others depend on) and a private BODY. On re-run, if a leaf's body changed but its signature is byte-identical, the dirty flag STOPS at that leaf — dependents aren't invalidated because nothing observable changed. Only a signature change punches through the firewall and dirties downstream consumers. The cockpit visualizes the invalidation wave BEFORE spending: 'this 4-word change rebuilds 11 leaves.' **Why better:** Naive dirty-marking re-cascades a whole subtree whenever any ancestor is touched, defeating incrementality. Incremental compilers (Rust's Salsa query system) gate invalidation on the observable interface, not the implementation — so a deep edit that changes no contract stays contained, and re-runs are cheap in the common case where the user changes 'how,' not 'what.'
- **Three-way merge: machine output and human edits are sibling branches the factory rebases** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Treat every artifact region as a git three-way merge: base = what the factory last generated, theirs = the new generation, ours = the human's local edits since. The factory generates into a shadow worktree and rebases the human's hand-edits on top of its regeneration, surfacing only true conflicts as merge markers. Local edits aren't preserved by luck — they're a branch the machine is contractually obligated to rebase. **Why better:** The current model silently clobbers between-run human edits. The factory already builds in git worktrees — it has the merge machinery, just isn't pointing it at the human's edits. This reframes 'the factory owns the file' into 'the factory is one contributor among two,' the difference between a toy and something you can live inside an edit loop with.
- **Edit provenance fences — declared HUMAN-OWNED regions the swarm physically cannot rewrite (VFX conform)** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Let any artifact carry machine-readable provenance fences marking regions MACHINE-GENERATED vs HUMAN-OWNED (locked). On re-run the worker is contractually forbidden from rewriting locked regions; it conforms its new output around them, the way a VFX conform reassembles new renders around locked, approved shots. Unlocking is an explicit user act, logged in the manifest. **Why better:** Three-way merge resolves accidental collisions; provenance fences PREVENT them by making 'the human owns this' a declared, durable boundary the swarm can't cross. Film pipelines never re-render an approved locked shot — they conform around it. A guarantee stronger than 'we'll try to merge.'
- **Pin / freeze any node — human-blessed subtrees become byte-immutable, conflict-on-collision** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Let the user pin any node ('this floor is perfect, never touch it'). A pinned node is byte-locked across all future runs regardless of upstream contract changes — the factory routes around it, and if an upstream change would force it to change, it raises a conflict instead of silently regenerating.
