Generalizes ArtLab's byte-diff protection on Otis/CEO/Mara assets from a hardcoded allowlist to a user-facing primitive. **Why better:** Hashing handles the common case, but humans want a hard guarantee for the parts they're happy with ('do NOT touch the auth floor'). An explicit lock gives a deterministic promise no nondeterministic worker can override — strictly safer than hoping the hash stays put. The codebase already byte-protects blessed assets via CI.
- **Edits reverse-propagate UP the tree — a hand-edit becomes a proposed intent/contract change** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — When a human hand-edits leaf code, the factory runs the build backwards: infer what contract/intent change that edit IMPLIES and propose lifting it into the plan-tree ('you renamed this field everywhere — promote to the schema contract?'). The human edit becomes a first-class intent signal that steers the build instead of a clobber-risk to defend against. **Why better:** Closes the loop the fire-once model can't even see: today human edits are friction to avoid destroying; here they become the steering input. The iterative 'now change this one thing' is handled by editing the artifact directly, and the tree catches up.
- **Two-key reconciler — a re-run proposes a reviewable diff and never writes directly** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — A re-run never writes. It produces a PROPOSED DIFF against current on-disk reality (which includes human edits since last run) and the cockpit shows it as a reviewable changeset — added/changed/removed/preserved per node, plus contract conflicts needing a call — that the human applies, partially applies, or rejects. 'Apply' is the only write path, mirroring ArtLab's reconciler-as-single-read-path discipline and Terraform's plan/apply split. **Why better:** Makes every re-run safe-by-construction: nothing is clobbered because the output is a proposal, not a fact, until a human commits it. Turns the terrifying 'rebuild' into a PR-style review — exactly the mental model users already trust for iterative change (codemods, dependabot, migrations).
- **Cockpit green-wave replay colors reused vs rebuilt vs merged nodes on the live tree** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — On a re-run, render the plan-tree tinted by each node's fate — gray for reused/unchanged, amber for dirtied-by-dependency, green for actively rebuilt, blue for human-edited-and-merged. The same green wave that climbs on a first build now visibly shows what the second run chose to leave alone. **Why better:** Without it a re-run looks identical to a fresh build and the user can't tell preserved from regenerated, so they can't trust the reuse. Making reuse visible is what lets a human believe 'it really only changed the one thing' instead of re-diffing the whole repo by hand.
- **Persist the decision-trace, not the bytes, as cross-run truth — re-runs diff decisions** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — The durable record of a run isn't the files — it's an append-only ledger of the DECISIONS each node made (why this name, why this shape, which alternative was rejected, what taste signal applied). On re-run the factory diffs decision-traces, not bytes. A node rebuilds only if a decision it depended on actually changed; cosmetic byte-drift is invisible because bytes were never the source of truth. **Why better:** Solves 'what was decided vs incidental' — the real reason fresh-from-intent feels safe. ArtLab's taste-ledger that 'carries forward into future runs' is a baby version; generalize so EVERY node has provenance and re-runs become decision-diffs.
- **Run snapshots + instant rollback and time-travel scrubber (event-sourced lot tracking)** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Persist each run as an immutable, addressable SNAPSHOT of the full tree + artifacts + manifest, like a manufacturing lot with a genealogy record. The cockpit gets a video-editor scrubhead across the artifact's entire history: drag back to run 3, fork a new timeline from there, diff any two points as a visual plan-tree morph, or roll one subtree back to a prior good run. Nothing is destroyed; runs are an append-only ledger — the artifact is a 4D object you scrub through. **Why better:** Fire-once leaves no escape hatch when a re-run makes things worse — you can't compare, revert, or bisect. Event-sourced lot tracking (and the Tower's own ledger/save-point culture) makes a bad re-build one slider-drag away from undone, and you can always answer 'what did run N-1 actually produce here.'
- **Speculative shadow-builds — pre-bake the likely next edit before you ask (branch prediction)** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Between runs, idle workers speculatively explore the most-likely next intent-edits (the cockpit knows you tweak copy after layout, schema after model) and pre-compute those subtrees in shadow worktrees. When you actually make the edit, the rebuild is already done and just gets promoted — the second run feels instantaneous because it ran before you asked. **Why better:** The current model makes you wait for a cold rebuild every iteration; this hides the edit-loop latency entirely by spending idle compute on the future. It weaponizes 'more processes = more power' toward speed, turning a stop-and-wait cycle into a feels-live editing surface.
- **The artifact files a bug report against its own intent when reality drifts (artifact-push)** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Invert graphify's verification: instead of you re-running to check, the as-built graph continuously watches the live artifact and, when reality diverges from the contract (a human hand-edited a frozen node, a dependency moved, a test now fails), the factory opens a ticket on ITSELF — 'node 4.2.1 drifted from its contract; reconcile, adopt-as-new-intent, or revert?' The re-run is triggered by the artifact noticing it's wrong, not by you remembering to ask. **Why better:** The current assumption is human-pull (you decide to re-run); this is artifact-push (the build tells you it needs a run and why). Drift is caught at the moment it happens with full causal context, instead of discovered as a mystery diff three runs later.
- **The Factory Never Stops — kill the run boundary; a reconciliation loop, not invocations** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Delete the invocation model entirely. The plan-tree is a long-lived daemon holding the whole artifact's intent, continuously reconciling reality against the contract graph the way a Kubernetes controller reconciles desired vs actual state. You don't 're-run' — you mutate the intent (edit a bullet, repoint a contract) and the disturbance ripples through the tree as a localized rebuild wave while everything else stays frozen by construction. 'Idempotent re-run' stops being a feature because there is no run boundary to be idempotent across. **Why better:** Reframes the entire problem out of existence: diffing two runs is hard, but a reconciliation loop never has two runs to diff — it only ever has drift to correct. Byte-stability becomes the default (untouched = unreconciled = untouched) instead of something you fight nondeterminism to preserve.
- **The plan-tree is the deliverable; code is a recompilable, disposable projection** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Invert what's durable. Keep the plan-tree (intent → sections → leaves → contracts) as the canonical, versioned artifact, and treat generated code as a disposable projection re-emittable from the tree at any time. A 'change one thing' edit is a structured edit to a node, which recompiles only its subtree's projection. The vision already builds the tree every run and throws it away — this keeps it and makes it the spine. **Why better:** Re-runs stop being 'rebuild from fuzzy intent' and become 'recompile from a precise, diffable tree.' Diffing two plan-trees is tractable; diffing two intents is not.
- **Append-only immutable builds — there is no 'second run,' every run births a new content-keyed build** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Reject in-place idempotent re-runs in favor of strict append-only immutability. You never mutate a built tree; each invocation produces a NEW immutable build keyed by content hash, and 'change one thing' is just a new build that shares most content-addressed leaves with the prior one (reused by hash, never regenerated). The old build still exists, untouched, forever. **Why better:** 'Idempotent re-run against an evolving target' quietly assumes mutation-in-place, which is exactly what makes preserving human edits and byte-stability painful. Append-only builds make byte-stability automatic and human edits a first-class new input rather than something to rescue from clobbering. Git and Nix prove the model works.
- **The unit of idempotency is the LEAF cache, not the run — make leaves pure functions** `big/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Drop run-level idempotency entirely and push it down to the leaf. Every leaf becomes a pure function of (its frozen contract + its inputs), wrapped in a memoization cache keyed on that tuple. 'Run-over-run' stops being a concept — there's just a warm cache: an unchanged leaf returns its byte-identical cached output for free; a changed contract is a cache miss that rebuilds only that leaf and its dependents. **Why better:** Dissolves the entire aspect into a solved problem (Bazel/Turborepo/Nix build caching) and kills the 'nondeterministic worker silently regenerates an unchanged subtree' fear — cache hits are byte-stable by definition, no tree-diffing reconciler needed. The hard problem becomes 'make leaves pure,' which contract-freezing is already 90% toward.
- **Fold run-over-run diffing into graphify — no separate diff subsystem, only graph reconciliation** `small/reasonable` _(curated)_ — Don't build run-over-run diffing as its own thing. graphify already maintains the as-built verification graph (does reality match the contract graph?). A 're-run' is just feeding new intent into graphify and letting the SAME drift-detection that catches as-built mismatches decide what's stale. 'Diff between prior tree and new tree' collapses into 'nodes where the graph says reality diverges from the new contract.' **Why better:** Two separate systems that both answer 'what changed and what needs rebuilding?' is redundant and will disagree. graphify is already the source of truth for contract-vs-reality; folding re-run diffing into it removes a whole conceptual surface and guarantees the rebuild decision and verification decision can never contradict each other.
- **Kill run-over-run diffing entirely: the factory is fire-once, your editor is for edits** `big/rash` _(curated)_ — Delete the notion of a second factory run against a built tree. Once an artifact is built and a human touches it, it stops being a factory artifact and becomes ordinary source code — you edit it with your normal editor/agent, not by re-invoking the swarm. The factory only ever runs from scratch on empty ground; 'change one thing' is a category error it should refuse. **Why better:** The reconciler (diff prior tree, preserve human edits, keep subtrees byte-stable) may be more complex than the factory itself and is the classic source of 'silently clobbered my work' horror. Drawing a hard line — factory births, humans/agents raise — deletes the hardest subsystem entirely and routes iteration to tools that already solve it (git, a coding agent).
- **Forbid human edits — factory output is read-only between runs, edits go upstream into intent** `small/rash` _(curated)_ — Invert the 'preserve local human edits' goal: make factory output read-only, checked in as generated and gated like ArtLab's byte-protected assets. To change something you change the INTENT or CONTRACT and re-run — never the output directly. Human edits to generated files are rejected by CI, not lovingly merged. **Why better:** 'Preserve human edits' is the single hardest, most failure-prone requirement and it fights the factory's premise that intent is the source of truth. If output is editable, intent and artifact silently diverge and every re-run is a 3-way merge nightmare. Forcing edits upstream keeps a single source of truth and makes re-runs trivially safe — the byte-diff CI machinery already exists to enforce this.
- **Re-runs rebuild EVERYTHING by default — selective reuse is the premature optimization** `small/rash` _(curated)_ — Invert the reuse instinct. Default behavior of a second run is a total from-scratch rebuild of the whole tree; selective reuse is an opt-in flag for the impatient. Trust the deterministic-enough contracts + tests to make a full rebuild converge to an equivalent artifact, and let cheap parallel compute eat the cost. **Why better:** Partial reuse is precisely where subtle staleness bugs hide (a reused subtree silently depends on a contract that moved two levels up). A full rebuild is dumb, obviously-correct, and embarrassingly parallel — the factory's whole superpower. 'More processes = more power' means recompute is cheap; correctness-via-simplicity beats a clever-but-leaky reuse cache.

## Completeness critic — what we may have missed

**Missed aspects:**
- THE INTENT-CAPTURE FRONT DOOR ITSELF. Every aspect downstream of 'intent in' was brainstormed, but nobody brainstormed how intent actually gets specified. The whole tree is derived from an initial fuzzy prompt — yet there's no aspect for intent elicitation, disambiguation, or the 'wrong intent compiles perfectly' failure. The factory can build a flawless artifact for the wrong thing. Garbage-in is the single highest-leverage failure mode and it has no dimension. (Existing 'grill-me' is the intent-sharpening front door — the factory has no analog and nobody noticed.)
- TIME, DEADLINES, AND WALL-CLOCK SCHEDULING. Every aspect treats the run as 'spend until done.' Nothing addresses: time budgets (vs token budgets), deadlines, 'I need a shippable version by 3pm,' run duration estimation, or the latency/throughput tradeoff of more-processes-vs-coordination-overhead. A factory with no clock can't be trusted with anything real-world-scheduled.
- CONCURRENCY CORRECTNESS OF THE ORCHESTRATOR ITSELF (not just write serialization). 'Shared-resource contention' was named, but the orchestrator is a distributed system: manifest as shared mutable state, race conditions between the dispatcher and N workers, partial manifest writes, lost updates, the 'two workers claim the same leaf' problem, crash of the MAIN agent mid-run (who resumes the resumer?). The meta-process has no supervision story.
- DETERMINISM/NON-DETERMINISM OF THE TREE STRUCTURE. 'Same intent twice' was named only for output reproducibility. Deeper: the PLAN-TREE itself is LLM-generated and non-deterministic. Two runs may decompose the SAME intent into structurally DIFFERENT trees with different contracts. The whole edifice assumes the decomposition is the stable ground truth, but it's the softest, most variable layer.
- MULTI-TENANCY / CONCURRENT RUNS. Every aspect assumes ONE run at a time. What happens when two factory runs touch the same repo simultaneously? Worktree collision, manifest collision, branch-name collision, graph staleness across runs. The forge/ArtLab daemon is long-lived — concurrent invocation is inevitable and unmodeled.
- OBSERVABILITY OF WORKER INTERNAL STATE, not just node status. The cockpit shows plan-tree + status + tokens. It does NOT show: what a stuck worker is actually THINKING, why a leaf is looping, a worker that's confidently wrong, or the live transcript of a headless 'claude -p'. 'Status: building' for 20 minutes is a black box. Debuggability of a swarm you can't see into is unaddressed.
- THE HUMAN-IN-MIDDLE EXPERTISE / TASTE INJECTION. Gates are framed as approve/reject scope and direction. But for a deck, a research report, a decision — the value is often a single piece of taste/judgment the human holds that no contract can encode ('actually, lead with the revenue number'). There's no aspect for injecting qualitative judgment that ISN'T a gate and isn't a spec.
- DATA / FIXTURES / SEED STATE for the build to run against. Tests need data. A 'failing test' presupposes fixtures, a seeded DB, mock external services, API keys for integration tests. The contracts layer freezes signatures+schema+tests but nobody asked where the RUNTIME ENVIRONMENT and test data come from. (This repo literally has scripts/seed-owner-data.ts — the factory has no fixtures dimension.)
- NON-CODE ARTIFACT VERIFICATION. The generality claim ('factory for anything') collides with the verification model, which is entirely code-shaped (failing tests, green wave, tsc). What is 'green' for a DECK, a RESEARCH REPORT, a DECISION, an ART CAMPAIGN? These have no compiler. The oracle problem was named ONLY for code; for 80% of the claimed generality there is no oracle at all and nobody flagged it.

**Missed ideas:**
- A DRY-RUN / SIMULATION MODE that builds the FULL plan-tree and contracts but executes ZERO workers — outputs the predicted cost, time, file-touch surface, and risk hotspots. The 'scope gate' is a coarse yes/no; this is a flight simulator for the run. Lets the human inspect the contract graph BEFORE a single token is spent on building. (Adversarial-review-the-plan exists for plans; nothing simulates the BUILD.)
- CONTRACTS AS A FIRST-CLASS, HUMAN-EDITABLE, VERSIONED ARTIFACT — a 'contract IDE.' Instead of frozen-top-down-then-autonomous, the human edits the typed signatures / schema / test stubs DIRECTLY in the cockpit before unfreezing. The contract becomes the steering wheel. Radical inversion: the human's job isn't prompting, it's editing the spec graph.
- SPECULATIVE / BRANCHING EXECUTION. When a leaf is ambiguous or the router is uncertain, build 2-3 variants IN PARALLEL (Claude's take + Codex's take), then let a judge pick the green one — like speculative execution in a CPU. Quota failover was framed as fallback; this uses the dual-model budget for redundancy-as-quality, not just resilience.
- A 'BLAST RADIUS' / REVERSIBILITY TIER orthogonal to the altitude dial. Altitude = how BIG. Blast radius = how DANGEROUS/IRREVERSIBLE (touches payments? migrations? prod data? deletes files?). A T0 component that drops a DB column is more dangerous than a T3 greenfield app. Verification depth and human gates should key off blast radius, NOT size. The dial conflates magnitude with risk.
- RUN-AS-A-DIFF / PROPOSAL MODE: the factory's output is NEVER applied directly — it always lands as a reviewable proposal (a PR, a diff, a staged branch) the human merges. This makes 'building INTO a live system' safe by construction and makes idempotent re-runs natural. The hypothesis assumes the factory WRITES; safer framing is the factory PROPOSES.
- A LIBRARY OF FROZEN, REUSABLE SUBTREES ('factory parts'). When the factory builds 'a Stripe webhook with idempotency' once and it goes green, that whole subtree+contract+tests becomes a cached, parameterizable MACRO it pattern-matches on next time — skip re-deriving. The plan-tree becomes compounding capital, not disposable. (Closest existing analog: ArtLab Asset Packs — promoted, reusable. The code factory has no Asset-Pack equivalent.)
- AN ADVERSARIAL 'RED TEAM' WORKER whose ONLY job is to try to BREAK the green wave — write tests that SHOULD pass but don't, find the contract's blind spots, attack the artifact. Distinct from the Codex reviewer (which checks the diff). This attacks the ORACLE itself — the thing everyone trusts. Catches 'all tests green but the tests are wrong.'
- TASTE / STYLE TRANSFER from the existing codebase as an automatic contract input. Before building, the factory mines the repo for its conventions (this repo's CLAUDE.md has 30+ hard rules: no `any`, REST-not-Drizzle, gsap-init contract, Tailwind v3) and compiles them into per-leaf lint contracts so workers can't violate house style. Convention-as-contract, auto-extracted, not hand-fed.
- A 'STOP-LOSS' / CIRCUIT BREAKER on the run: declarative kill conditions ('abort if cost > $40,' 'abort if any worker fails 3x,' 'abort if the green-wave stalls 10 min,' 'abort if a worker touches public/lobby/bg-*.jpg'). Autonomy with no automatic abort is a runaway-spend / runaway-damage hazard. The protected-files concept from ArtLab generalizes to a guardrail layer.
- INTERACTIVE BISECTION OF A RED TREE. When the green wave stalls, the cockpit auto-bisects to the lowest failing leaf and offers: retry / re-decompose / hand-to-human / mark-shippable-without. Turns 'the run failed' into a navigable, surgical recovery UI instead of a restart.
- THE FACTORY EMITS ITS OWN MAINTENANCE CONTRACT. Beyond building the artifact, it outputs the runbook, the rollback script, the monitoring it needs, and the 'how to extend this' doc — so the artifact is operable AFTER the run ends. A factory that builds but leaves no operating manual produces orphans.

**Unchallenged assumptions:**
- THAT TOP-DOWN DECOMPOSITION CONVERGES. The core flow — recursive plan-tree, contracts frozen top-down, build bottom-up — assumes a fuzzy intent cleanly decomposes into independent leaves whose contracts compose. Most genuinely hard work is NOT cleanly decomposable; the hard part is the cross-cutting concern that lives BETWEEN leaves (auth, error handling, perf, consistency). The factory optimizes the part that was already easy (parallel leaves) and structurally cannot see the part that's actually hard (the integration). Nobody challenged that decomposability is the exception, not the rule.
- THAT 'FROZEN CONTRACTS' IS THE RIGHT DEFAULT. One aspect ('contract renegotiation when a leaf proves the spec wrong') gestures at this but treats it as an exception path. The deeper unchallenged claim is that freezing FIRST is even correct. In real building, the spec is discovered DURING construction — the leaf teaches you the contract was wrong. A waterfall-of-contracts may be the wrong paradigm entirely, and renegotiation may be the COMMON case, not the edge.
- THAT MORE PARALLELISM = MORE POWER. Stated as a near-axiom ('more processes = more power'). Unchallenged: coordination cost, merge-conflict explosion, context-fragmentation (each worker has a keyhole view), and the integration tax grow SUPERLINEARLY with worker count. Beyond some N, more workers produce a less coherent artifact, faster. Nobody asked where the optimum is or whether it's often N=1.
- THAT THE TWO-MODEL ROUTER ('Claude architects the fuzzy top, Codex builds explicit leaves') IS A REAL DIVISION OF LABOR rather than an org-chart fiction. It's asserted as architecture but never justified empirically. Maybe Codex architects better on some domains; maybe a single model with more context beats two models with handoff-loss between them. The handoff itself LOSES information (the leaf-builder lacks the architect's why). Cross-model handoff cost is unexamined.
- THAT GENERALITY IS FREE — 'factory for anything decomposable.' The verification model, the contracts (typed signatures + DB schema + tests), the green-wave, the worktrees, the stitch are ALL code-shaped. A deck, a decision, a research report share the WORD 'decompose' but share none of the machinery. The honest version is 'a code factory with a thin veneer over other modalities.' Nobody challenged whether 'anything' is real or marketing — and the existing ArtLab proves art needed its OWN bespoke pipeline, not the code one.
- THAT THE HUMAN WANTS TO BE OUT OF THE LOOP ('zero human interaction mid-run' as the goal). For high-stakes, irreversible, or taste-driven work, the human WANTS to be in the loop continuously — autonomy is a liability, not a feature. The system optimizes for absence-of-human when the actual need is often presence-with-leverage. 'Mid-run steering' was listed as an aspect but the GOAL of zero-interaction was never itself questioned.
- THAT THE PLAN-TREE IS THE RIGHT DATA STRUCTURE. A tree assumes strict hierarchy and no shared dependencies between siblings. Real systems are GRAPHS — leaf A and leaf C both depend on leaf B's contract; a shared type is referenced from five places. 'graphify' is bolted on for knowledge lookup, but the PLAN itself is forced into a tree it doesn't fit. The dependency structure is a DAG; modeling it as a tree guarantees the stitch phase fights the actual topology.
- THAT 'GREEN' MEANS CORRECT. The oracle problem was named, but the whole architecture still treats the green wave as ground truth that triggers the stitch and the done-claim. Tests passing means 'consistent with the tests I wrote,' which for LLM-authored tests means 'consistent with my own possibly-wrong understanding.' Self-authored tests verifying self-authored code is a closed loop that can be confidently, totally wrong — and the factory's confidence will be HIGHEST exactly when it's most wrong.
- THAT THIS SHOULD BE BUILT AT ALL / BUILD-VS-BUY-VS-WAIT. Nobody challenged the premise. This is a massive infrastructure investment for a solo senior CS student whose actual product is The Tower (an internship app). The opportunity cost is enormous, frontier labs are shipping convergent autonomy (agent swarms, Claude Code's own subagents) that may obsolete a bespoke orchestrator within months, and the existing forge + worktrees + ArtLab already cover the 80% case. The hypothesis assumes the factory is worth building; the strongest critique is that the user's own product is the thing being starved to build a tool to build products.
- THAT INTENT IS STABLE FOR THE DURATION OF A RUN. The flow is intent-in → autonomous build → artifact-out, but on any run long enough to be worth parallelizing, the human's understanding of what they want CHANGES as they see partial results. The factory assumes a fixed target; real creative/build work has a moving target. A system that locks intent at t=0 and spends an hour is optimizing against a spec the human has already outgrown by the time it finishes.
